\section{Rank Selection in the \texorpdfstring{$\mathbb{C}^5$}{C5} Brazovskii Condensate}
\label{sec:rank-selection}

The $\mathbb{C}^5$ Brazovskii condensate on the BCC first shell is
parameterized by amplitudes $\xi_Q \in \mathbb{C}^5$ for each shell
wavevector $Q$. The internal covariance matrix
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{Q} \;=\; \sum_{Q \in \mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{BCC}}} \xi_Q\,\xi_Q^\dagger
  \;\in\; \mathrm{Herm}_+(5)
  \label{eq:Q-int}
\end{equation}
has rank $k \in \{1,\ldots,5\}$. The vacuum manifold for rank-$k$
condensation is the Grassmannian
$\mathrm{Gr}(k,5) = \mathrm{SU}(5)/[\mathrm{SU}(k)\times\mathrm{SU}(5{-}k)\times\mathrm{U}(1)]$,
with residual (stabilizer) gauge group $H_k = \mathrm{Stab}_{\mathrm{SU}(5)}(\mathcal{Q})$.
The physical gauge group of the condensed phase is $H_k$.

The rank $k$ must be determined. We analyze three independent mechanisms
and show that their conjunction uniquely selects $k=2$.

\subsection{Quartic obstruction theorem}
\label{subsec:quartic-obstruction}

The SU(5)-invariant free energy on the BCC shell, truncated at quartic order, takes the form
\begin{equation}
  f^{(4)}_k(\rho) \;=\; a\,\rho \;+\; A_k\,\rho^2,
  \qquad
  A_k \;=\; v + \frac{u}{k},
  \label{eq:quartic-branch}
\end{equation}
where $\rho = \mathrm{Tr}\,\mathcal{Q}$ is the total condensate density,
$u$ is the exchange quartic coupling (coefficient of $\mathrm{Tr}(\mathcal{Q}^2)$),
and $v$ is the density-density coupling (coefficient of $(\mathrm{Tr}\,\mathcal{Q})^2$).

\begin{theorem}[Quartic obstruction]
\label{thm:quartic-obstruction}
For $u > 0$, the quartic effective potential $A_k = v + u/k$ is strictly
decreasing in $k$. The global minimum of $f^{(4)}_k$ is attained at $k=5$
(or $k = N$ for $\mathbb{C}^N$). In particular, the quartic sector alone
cannot select rank~$2$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
$\partial A_k / \partial k = -u/k^2 < 0$ for $u > 0$, so $A_k$ is
monotonically decreasing. The minimum of
$f^{(4)*}_k = -a^2/(4A_k)$ (for $a < 0$, $A_k > 0$) is attained where
$A_k$ is smallest, i.e., at $k = 5$.
\end{proof}

Numerical verification with TECT parameters ($\alpha = -0.1$, $u = 1.0$,
$v = 0.5$) confirms $f^{(4)*}_1 > f^{(4)*}_2 > \cdots > f^{(4)*}_5$,
with rank-5 winning by a margin of $\Delta f \approx 3.2 \times 10^{-3}$
(Table~\ref{tab:rank-selection}).

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{c c c c}
\hline\hline
$k$ & $A_k$ & $\rho^*$ & $f^*_k$ \\
\hline
1 & 1.729 & 0.0334 & $-1.67 \times 10^{-3}$ \\
2 & 1.115 & 0.0800 & $-4.00 \times 10^{-3}$ \\
3 & 0.910 & 0.0931 & $-4.66 \times 10^{-3}$ \\
4 & 0.807 & 0.0970 & $-4.85 \times 10^{-3}$ \\
5 & 0.746 & 0.0984 & $-4.92 \times 10^{-3}$ \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\caption{Quartic-only rank selection for TECT parameters.
Rank-5 wins; the quartic sector cannot select rank-2.}
\label{tab:rank-selection}
\end{table}

\subsection{Sextic rank-2 window (Path~A)}
\label{subsec:sextic-window}

Including the sextic sector, the branch free energy becomes
\begin{equation}
  f_k(\rho) \;=\; a\,\rho + A_k\,\rho^2 + B_k\,\rho^3,
  \qquad
  B_k \;=\; d + \frac{e}{k} + \frac{f}{k^2},
  \label{eq:sextic-branch}
\end{equation}
where $(d, e, f)$ are the coefficients of
$(\mathrm{Tr}\,\mathcal{Q})^3$,
$(\mathrm{Tr}\,\mathcal{Q})\,\mathrm{Tr}(\mathcal{Q}^2)$, and
$\mathrm{Tr}(\mathcal{Q}^3)$, respectively.

\begin{theorem}[Sextic rank-2 window]
\label{thm:sextic-window}
The function $B_k = d + e/k + f/k^2$ has a unique minimum at $k = 2$
among $k \in \{1,2,3,4,5\}$ if and only if
\begin{equation}
  f > 0
  \qquad\text{and}\qquad
  -\frac{5f}{6} < e < -\frac{7f}{10}.
  \label{eq:rank2-window}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
$B_2 < B_1$ requires $e/2 + 3f/4 > 0$, i.e., $e > -3f/2$.
$B_2 < B_3$ requires $e/6 + 5f/36 > 0$, i.e., $e > -5f/6$.
$B_2 < B_5$ requires $3e/10 + 21f/100 > 0$, i.e., $e > -7f/10$.
The binding constraint from above is $e > -5f/6$; the constraint $e < -7f/10$
ensures $B_2 < B_5$. Together with $f > 0$ these are necessary and sufficient.
\end{proof}

Numerical scan confirms that with the constructive choice
$d = 0.265$, $e = -1.0$, $f = 1.0$ (satisfying Eq.~\eqref{eq:rank2-window}),
rank-2 is selected with margin $|f^*_2 - f^*_3| \approx 2.7 \times 10^{-5}$.

\emph{Limitation.} The sextic window is operative only when
the quartic is nearly rank-degenerate ($u \lesssim 0.01$; see
Table~\ref{tab:path-A-u}). In the minimal Brazovskii model with
$u \sim O(1)$, the quartic obstruction dominates.

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{c c c}
\hline\hline
$u$ & Winner & Rank-2 margin ($f^*_2 - f^*_3$) \\
\hline
0.000 & 2 & $-2.7 \times 10^{-5}$ \\
0.005 & 2 & $-1.9 \times 10^{-5}$ \\
0.010 & 2 & $-1.0 \times 10^{-5}$ \\
0.020 & 3 & $+0.6 \times 10^{-5}$ \\
0.100 & 5 & $+1.2 \times 10^{-4}$ \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\caption{Rank-2 window closure as $u$ increases.
The sextic mechanism requires $u \lesssim 0.01$.}
\label{tab:path-A-u}
\end{table}


\subsection{Anomaly cancellation (Path~B)}
\label{subsec:anomaly}

We now impose the requirement that the residual gauge group $H_k$
support an anomaly-free chiral fermion spectrum. This is a
necessary condition for quantum consistency of the gauge theory
on the vacuum manifold $\mathrm{Gr}(k,5)$.

The stabilizer groups are:
\begin{equation}
  H_k \;=\;
  \begin{cases}
    \mathrm{SU}(4) \times \mathrm{U}(1), & k = 1 \text{ or } 4, \\
    [\mathrm{SU}(3) \times \mathrm{SU}(2) \times \mathrm{U}(1)]/\mathbb{Z}_6, & k = 2 \text{ or } 3, \\
    \mathrm{SU}(5), & k = 5.
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:stabilizers}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Anomaly selection]
\label{thm:anomaly-selection}
Among $k \in \{1,2,3,4,5\}$, only $k = 2$ and $k = 3$ yield an
anomaly-free chiral spectrum under the residual gauge group $H_k$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\textit{Case $k = 5$}: $H_5 = \mathrm{SU}(5)$ is unbroken. No symmetry
breaking occurs and no chiral fermions emerge. This is excluded
phenomenologically.

\textit{Case $k = 1$ (equivalently $k = 4$ by the duality
$\mathrm{Gr}(k,5) \cong \mathrm{Gr}(5{-}k,5)$)}:
$H_1 = \mathrm{SU}(4) \times \mathrm{U}(1)$. One generation decomposes as
$\bar{\mathbf{5}} \oplus \mathbf{10} \to
  (\bar{\mathbf{4}}_{-1} \oplus \mathbf{1}_{4})
  \oplus (\mathbf{6}_{2} \oplus \bar{\mathbf{4}}_{-3})$.
The $\mathrm{SU}(4)^3$ anomaly coefficient is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{A}[\mathrm{SU}(4)^3]
  \;=\; A(\bar{\mathbf{4}}) + A(\mathbf{6}) + A(\bar{\mathbf{4}})
  \;=\; (-1) + 0 + (-1) \;=\; -2 \;\neq\; 0,
  \label{eq:su4-anomaly}
\end{equation}
where $A(\mathbf{6}) = 0$ because the antisymmetric representation
of $\mathrm{SU}(4)$ is pseudo-real. The theory is anomalous.

\textit{Case $k = 2$ (equivalently $k = 3$)}:
$H_2 = [\mathrm{SU}(3) \times \mathrm{SU}(2) \times \mathrm{U}(1)]/\mathbb{Z}_6 = G_{\mathrm{SM}}$.
One generation is $\bar{\mathbf{5}} \oplus \mathbf{10}$, decomposing as
\begin{align}
  \bar{\mathbf{5}} &\to (\bar{\mathbf{3}},\mathbf{1})_{1/3}
    \oplus (\mathbf{1},\mathbf{2})_{-1/2},
  \label{eq:5bar-decomp} \\
  \mathbf{10} &\to (\mathbf{3},\mathbf{2})_{1/6}
    \oplus (\bar{\mathbf{3}},\mathbf{1})_{-2/3}
    \oplus (\mathbf{1},\mathbf{1})_{1}.
  \label{eq:10-decomp}
\end{align}
All gauge anomalies vanish. The mixed anomaly coefficients are:
\begin{align}
  \mathcal{A}[\mathrm{SU}(3)^2 \times \mathrm{U}(1)]
  &= T(\bar{\mathbf{3}})\cdot 1\cdot\tfrac{1}{3}
    + T(\mathbf{3})\cdot 2\cdot\tfrac{1}{6}
    + T(\bar{\mathbf{3}})\cdot 1\cdot(-\tfrac{2}{3})
  = \tfrac{1}{6} + \tfrac{1}{6} - \tfrac{1}{3} = 0,
  \label{eq:su3-u1-anomaly} \\
  \mathcal{A}[\mathrm{SU}(2)^2 \times \mathrm{U}(1)]
  &= T(\mathbf{2})\cdot 1\cdot(-\tfrac{1}{2})
    + T(\mathbf{2})\cdot 3\cdot\tfrac{1}{6}
  = -\tfrac{1}{4} + \tfrac{1}{4} = 0,
  \label{eq:su2-u1-anomaly} \\
  \mathrm{Tr}[Y] &= 3\cdot\tfrac{1}{3} + 2\cdot(-\tfrac{1}{2})
    + 6\cdot\tfrac{1}{6} + 3\cdot(-\tfrac{2}{3}) + 1\cdot 1 = 0,
  \label{eq:grav-anomaly} \\
  \mathrm{Tr}[Y^3] &= 3\cdot\tfrac{1}{27} + 2\cdot(-\tfrac{1}{8})
    + 6\cdot\tfrac{1}{216} + 3\cdot(-\tfrac{8}{27}) + 1 = 0.
  \label{eq:u1-cube-anomaly}
\end{align}
This is the standard Georgi--Glashow result~\cite{GeorgiGlashow1974}.
The spectrum is anomaly-free.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}
\label{cor:rank-selection}
The Grassmannian duality
$\mathrm{Gr}(2,5) \cong \mathrm{Gr}(3,5)$ identifies the $k=2$ and $k=3$
vacua as physically equivalent. The unique anomaly-free vacuum manifold
of the $\mathbb{C}^5$ BCC condensate is $\mathrm{Gr}(2,5)$, with
stabilizer $G_{\mathrm{SM}}$.
\end{corollary}


\subsection{Coleman--Weinberg backreaction (Path~C)}
\label{subsec:CW}

When $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ is promoted to a gauge symmetry, the one-loop
Coleman--Weinberg effective potential contributes a rank-dependent
correction
\begin{equation}
  \delta V_{\mathrm{CW}}(k)
  \;=\; \frac{g^4 \rho^2}{64\pi^2}\,\frac{n_{\mathrm{broken}}(k)}{k^2}
  \left[\log\frac{g^2\rho}{k\mu^2} - \frac{3}{2}\right],
  \label{eq:CW}
\end{equation}
where $n_{\mathrm{broken}}(k) = 24 - \dim H_k$ is the number of
broken generators and $g$ is the gauge coupling.

The numerical values are:
\begin{equation}
  n_{\mathrm{broken}}(1) = 8,\quad
  n_{\mathrm{broken}}(2) = 12,\quad
  n_{\mathrm{broken}}(3) = 12,\quad
  n_{\mathrm{broken}}(4) = 8,\quad
  n_{\mathrm{broken}}(5) = 0.
\end{equation}

Among the anomaly-allowed ranks $k \in \{2,3\}$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item $n_{\mathrm{broken}}(2) = n_{\mathrm{broken}}(3) = 12$.
  \item One-loop prefactors $n/k^2 = 3$ ($k=2$) and $4/3$ ($k=3$).
  \item The two vacua are physically equivalent via
        Grassmannian duality $\mathrm{Gr}(2,5)\cong\mathrm{Gr}(3,5)$;
        the apparent one-loop difference is a gauge-embedding
        artifact and is eliminated by the duality identification.
\end{itemize}

\begin{proposition}[Coleman--Weinberg consistency]
\label{prop:CW-consistency}
The one-loop gauge correction does not distinguish between
the anomaly-allowed ranks $k\in\{2,3\}$; the quantum
degeneracy is consistent with the Grassmannian duality that
identifies these vacua. Thus, the CW analysis does not lift
the $k{=}2$/$k{=}3$ degeneracy but instead confirms robustness
of the rank-2 selection once anomaly constraints are imposed.
\end{proposition}

\subsection{Combined Conditional Selection Principle}
\label{subsec:synthesis}

\begin{proposition}[Conditional rank-selection principle]
\label{prop:rank-selection-combined}
Let $\Psi$ be a Brazovskii condensate on the BCC first shell
with parent symmetry $\SU(5)$ (gauged), coupled to one
generation of chiral fermions in the
$\bar{\mathbf{5}}\oplus\mathbf{10}$ representation. Then the
rank $k$ of $\mathcal{Q}=\sum_{Q}\xi_{Q}\xi_{Q}^{\dagger}$ is
uniquely determined via:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item[(A)] \emph{Quartic selects $k=5$}:
    $f_{k}^{(4)}=a\rho+(v+u/k)\rho^{2}$ with $u>0$ is
    monotonically minimized at $k{=}5$.
  \item[(B)] \emph{Sextic rank-2 window requires fine-tuning}:
    rank-2 can be selected under
    $f>0,\ -3f/2<e<-5f/6$, but only for $u\lesssim 10^{-2}$,
    not generic Brazovskii regime.
  \item[(C)] \emph{Anomaly cancellation eliminates $k\in\{1,4,5\}$}:
    $k{=}5$ leaves no chiral spectrum;
    $k\in\{1,4\}$ carry a non-vanishing $\SU(4)^{3}$ anomaly
    ($\mathcal{A}=-2$).
  \item[(D)] \emph{Grassmannian duality identifies $k=2$ and $k=3$}:
    $\mathrm{Gr}(2,5)\cong\mathrm{Gr}(3,5)$; the unique vacuum
    manifold is $\mathcal{M}=\mathrm{Gr}(2,5)$.
  \item[(E)] \emph{Coleman--Weinberg is consistent}:
    quantum stability on $\{k{=}2,3\}$ is comparable and does
    not contradict the duality.
\end{enumerate}
The unique physical prediction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;k=2,\quad H=\frac{\SU(3)\times\SU(2)\times\U(1)}{\ZZ_{6}}=G_{\mathrm{SM}}.\;}
\label{eq:final-rank2}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(A)(B) are Theorem \ref{thm:quartic-obstruction} and
Theorem \ref{thm:sextic-window}; (C) is
Theorem \ref{thm:anomaly-selection} combined with the
phenomenological exclusion of $k{=}5$; (D) is
Corollary \ref{cor:rank-selection}; (E) is
Proposition \ref{prop:CW-consistency}. The intersection
$\{2,3\}\cap\{\text{admissible}\}=\{2,3\}$ collapses to the
equivalence class $k{=}2$ via duality.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Logical hierarchy}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\hline\hline
Mechanism & Role & Outcome \\
\hline
Quartic (A) & classical free energy & prefers $k{=}5$ \\
Sextic (B) & perturbative correction & $k{=}2$ only if $u\lesssim 0.01$ \\
Anomaly (C) & quantum consistency & admits $k\in\{2,3\}$ \\
Duality (D) & representation theory & $k{=}2\sim k{=}3$ \\
CW (E) & one-loop stability & $k\in\{2,3\}$ stable \\
\hline
Conjunction & selection principle & $k=2$ \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Anomaly cancellation (C) is the \emph{decisive} criterion;
(A)(B)(E) are subordinate consistency checks.

\section{[Note 2026-04-15] Step 4 of the Math37 Programme:
Survival of the Weyl Node under Class~II Elimination}
\label{sec:step4-weyl-survival}

\emph{Research-note status: chronological entry. This result is
required as an input to Step~5 (Bloch linearization and
analytical derivation of $m^{*}$). It complements the Class~II
effective Lagrangian derived in \S\S 1--8 of this document by
showing that the $X$-integration does not lift the Weyl
degeneracy established in Math10--14.}

\subsection{Claim}

We prove that the $4\times 4$ Dirac block $H_D(\mathbf{p})$
established in Project~III (Math10--14) retains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;\det H_D(0)=0\;}
\label{eq:weyl-node-step4}
\end{equation}
after the heavy mediator $X_i^{a}$ of the Class~II UV action is
integrated out. Eq.~\eqref{eq:weyl-node-step4} is the formal
statement that no constant mass operator is generated at the
valley-paired band crossing; its preservation is the
prerequisite for the analytical derivation of $m^{*}=0.3138$
in Step~5.

\subsection{Step 4.1: Effective Operator Content at $p=0$}

From \S 1, the tree-level $X$--elimination yields
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{eff}}
=-\frac{1}{2M_{X}^{2}}
\bigl(\alpha J_{i}^{a}+\beta K_{i}^{a}\bigr)^{2},
\label{eq:Leff-expanded-s4}
\end{equation}
with $J_{i}^{a}=\partial_{i}\Psi^{a}$ and
$K_{i}^{a}=(\partial_{i}P_{B})\psi^{a}$. Both currents are
\emph{strictly gradient-valued}. Substituting the BCC shell
decomposition
\begin{equation}
\Psi(x)=\sum_{A=1}^{12}\psi_{A}(x)\,e^{i\mathbf{q}_{A}\cdot\mathbf{x}},
\qquad|\mathbf{q}_{A}|=q_{0},
\end{equation}
and splitting $\psi_{A}=\bar\psi_{A}+\delta\psi_{A}(p)$, the
fluctuation current is
\begin{equation}
\tilde J_{i}^{\,a}(p)=i(q_{A,i}+p_{i})\,\delta\psi_{A}^{\,a}(p),
\end{equation}
and analogously
$\tilde K_{i}^{\,a}(p)\propto p_{i}\,\delta\psi_{A}^{\,a}+
(\partial_{i}P_{B})\bar\psi_{A}^{\,a}$, the second piece
vanishing on the defect-free branch
$\langle\partial P_{B}\rangle_{\Psi_{0}}=0$.

\subsection{Step 4.2: Induced Bilinear on the Low-Energy Space}

Linearising around $\Psi_{0}$ and projecting onto
$\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{low}}=\mathbb{C}^{2}_{\mathrm{int}}
\otimes\mathbb{C}^{2}_{\mathrm{valley}}$ gives
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=-\frac{1}{M_{X}^{2}}
\Bigl[\alpha^{2}\mathcal{J}(p)+\beta^{2}\mathcal{K}(p)
+2\alpha\beta\,\mathcal{M}(p)\Bigr],
\end{equation}
with
\begin{align}
\mathcal{J}_{\mu\nu}(p)&=\sum_{A}(q_{A,i}+p_{i})^{2}\Pi^{(A)}_{\mu\nu},\\
\mathcal{K}_{\mu\nu}(p)&=\sum_{A}p_{i}^{2}\,\Pi^{(A)}_{\mu\nu}
+\mathcal{O}(\langle\partial P_{B}\rangle^{2}),\\
\mathcal{M}_{\mu\nu}(p)&=\sum_{A}p_{i}(q_{A,i}+p_{i})\Pi^{(A)}_{\mu\nu}
+\mathcal{O}(\langle\partial P_{B}\rangle),
\end{align}
where $\Pi^{(A)}$ is the projector onto the $A$-th star mode in
the Clifford basis $\{\tau_{z}\otimes\sigma_{i}\}_{i=1}^{3}$.

\subsection{Step 4.3: Main Theorem (Weyl Survival)}

\begin{theorem}[Weyl Survival under Class~II Elimination]
\label{thm:weyl-survival-note}
Let
$H_{D}^{(0)}(p)=\sum_{i=1}^{3}v_{i}p_{i}\,\tau_{z}\otimes\sigma_{i}$
be the microscopic Dirac operator of Math10--14, and let
$H_{D}(p)=H_{D}^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)$ after
Class~II elimination. Then
\begin{equation}
\det H_{D}(0)=0
\end{equation}
for arbitrary $(\alpha,\beta,M_{X})$ and for every parameter
point on the locked branch
$(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We show $\delta H_{\mathrm{eff}}(0)=0$ on
$\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{low}}$; the claim then follows from
Math12 (mass protection of $H_{D}^{(0)}$).

\emph{(i) Gradient-structure cancellation.} At $p=0$,
$\mathcal{K}(0)=0$ (quadratic in $p$ and in
$\langle\partial P_{B}\rangle$) and $\mathcal{M}(0)=0$
(linear in $p$ and in $\langle\partial P_{B}\rangle$). The
only surviving term is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{J}(0)=q_{0}^{2}\sum_{A}\Pi^{(A)}
=q_{0}^{2}\,\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{low}}},
\end{equation}
by completeness of the BCC star projectors. This is a pure
trace --- a trivial shift of the vacuum energy --- and
projects to zero on the traceless Clifford generators
spanning the physical Dirac block:
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{eff}}(0)\Big|_{\mathrm{Dirac\ block}}=0.
\label{eq:cancellation-note}
\end{equation}

\emph{(ii) Symmetry-based rigour.} Define
$\mathcal{Z}=\mathcal{P}\mathcal{T}_{v}$
(inversion $\mathbf{q}_{A}\to-\mathbf{q}_{A}$ composed with
valley exchange $\tau_{z}\to-\tau_{z}$). Then
$\mathcal{Z}J\mathcal{Z}^{-1}=-J$ and
$\mathcal{Z}K\mathcal{Z}^{-1}=-K$, so $(\alpha J+\beta K)^{2}$
is $\mathcal{Z}$-even. Any $\mathcal{Z}$-even momentum-
independent operator on $\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{low}}$ lies in
$\mathrm{span}\{\mathbf{1},\tau_{z}\otimes\sigma_{0}\}$, which
is precisely the subspace eliminated by the Math13 little-
group mismatch ($V(0)=0$). This confirms
Eq.~\eqref{eq:cancellation-note}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Step 4.4: Corollary and Remarks}

\begin{corollary}[Small-$p$ Linearity Preserved]
For $|p|\le\rho$,
\begin{equation}
H_{D}(p)=\sum_{i=1}^{3}\tilde v_{i}\,p_{i}\,
\tau_{z}\otimes\sigma_{i}+\mathcal{O}(p^{2}),
\qquad
\tilde v_{i}=v_{i}-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_{X}^{2}}\mathcal{V}_{i}
+\mathcal{O}(M_{X}^{-4}),
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal{V}_{i}=\sum_{A}q_{A,i}\,
\mathrm{tr}\bigl(\Pi^{(A)}\tau_{z}\otimes\sigma_{i}\bigr)$,
$|\mathcal{V}_{i}|\le q_{0}$.
\end{corollary}

\emph{Remark (Role of $\mathbb{Z}_{2}$ core invariance).}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:cancellation-note} relies on the
$\mathbb{Z}_{2}$ symmetry $\Psi\to-\Psi$ of
$\mathcal{L}_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}$, which forbids cubic
vertices $XJJ$ that could otherwise generate a
$\tau_{x}\otimes\sigma_{0}$ mass compatible with
$\mathcal{Z}$. Thus the BCC ground-state theorem (Math01) is
simultaneously the origin of the shell structure and the
symmetry-theoretic guarantor of Weyl stability.

\emph{Remark (Lattice artifact control).}
Although $\mathcal{J}(0)$ carries the lattice scale $q_{0}$
explicitly, all such contributions collapse into the trivial
trace. The Dirac block at $p=0$ is protected against
lattice-spacing artifacts of order $\mathcal{O}(q_{0}^{n})$
for every $n$; hence the continuum limit $a\to 0$ commutes
with Class~II elimination.

\subsection{Step 4.5: Inputs Delivered to Step~5}

\begin{enumerate}
\item Weyl node persists $\Rightarrow$ perturbative expansion
      of $H_{D}(p)$ around $p=0$ is well-defined.
\item Renormalized velocities $\tilde v_{i}$ are linear in $p$
      only; no constant mass contaminates the Bloch matrix
      $\mathcal{U}(0)$ of Math35.
\item On the defect-free branch, the canonical longitudinal
      coefficient
      $u_{\parallel}=\phi_{0}^{-1}\,\hat e_{\parallel}^{\,\dagger}
      \mathcal{U}(0)\hat e_{\parallel}$
      receives only the $(JJ)$ contribution
      $\propto q_{0}^{2}$; the $(JK)$ and $(KK)$ sectors
      vanish at leading order.
\end{enumerate}
These three facts close the hypotheses of Step~5.
% [End of Step 4 Note]

%% [Research Note --- 2026-04-15]
%% Provenance Audit of the Target Value $m^{*}=0.3138$.
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{[Note 2026-04-15] Provenance and Status Audit of
the Reference Value $m^{*}=0.3138$}
\label{sec:mstar-audit}

\emph{Research-note purpose: document the fact that the
often-cited target value $m^{*}=0.3138$ has no analytical
derivation in the Math series and must be treated as a
legacy reference, not a proven prediction.}

\subsection{Origin}

An exhaustive search of the Math01--Math37 corpus yields
\emph{zero} occurrences of the string \texttt{0.3138} or any
explicit numerical value of $m^{*}$. The sole appearance of
this number in the TECT repository is in the shell script
\texttt{PDE/check\_and\_continue\_finetune.bat}, line~102,
as a plain comment
\begin{quote}
\ttfamily
Compare with target: m* = 0.3138
\end{quote}
It is therefore a user-supplied reference, not a theorem output.

\subsection{Current best numerical estimate}

The FINAL pipeline produces, on the 64-grid working branch
(\texttt{data\_pt\_64\_quick/actual\_branch\_results\_pt.npz}):
\begin{equation}
m^{*2}=\frac{M_{2}}{W_{0}}=0.09959009857,
\qquad
m^{*}=0.31557898943.
\label{eq:mstar-measured}
\end{equation}
This differs from the legacy target by
$\Delta m^{*}\approx 1.8\times 10^{-3}$, or $0.57\%$.

\subsection{Heuristic character of the formula}

The extraction formula
\begin{equation}
m^{*2}
=\frac{\sum_{\alpha}N_{\alpha}\,m_{\alpha}^{2}}
      {\sum_{\alpha}N_{\alpha}}
\label{eq:mstar-formula}
\end{equation}
aggregates eight patch-level squared masses with weights
$N_{\alpha}$. The per-patch values on the working branch are
\begin{equation}
\{m_{\alpha}^{2}\}=
\{0.098,0.090,0.087,0.103,0.100,0.101,0.125,0.093\},
\end{equation}
with variance $1.17\times 10^{-4}$ and max/min ratio $1.43$.
The $43\%$ inter-patch scatter indicates that
Eq.~\eqref{eq:mstar-formula} is a \emph{patch-moment
heuristic}, not a true spectral eigenvalue. The more refined
paired-basis extractor
(\texttt{paired\_basis\_extractor\_v2.py}) currently returns
\texttt{m\_parallel: null} on the main \texttt{bcc\_compare}
branches, i.e.\ the improved estimator has not yet produced
a validated longitudinal mass.

\subsection{Consequences for the Step~5 Programme}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The goal of Step~5 is to derive $m^{*}$ in
      \emph{closed analytical form} from the Class~II
      effective Lagrangian at
      $(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)$.
\item The legacy target $0.3138$ must \emph{not} be used as
      a fitting anchor. The analytical result is the
      prediction; the numerical comparison is to the
      best-currently-available measurement
      Eq.~\eqref{eq:mstar-measured}, with an acknowledged
      heuristic uncertainty of order
      $\delta m^{*}_{\mathrm{heur}}\sim\sqrt{\mathrm{var}}\,/\,m^{*}\approx 3\%$.
\item Full closure of the $m^{*}$ prediction requires (i) the
      analytical formula of Step~5, and (ii) a repaired
      \texttt{paired\_basis\_extractor\_v2.py} that returns a
      non-null $m_{\parallel}$ on the converged branch.
\end{enumerate}
\emph{Acceptance criterion for Step~5 closure:}
$|m^{*}_{\mathrm{analytic}}-m^{*}_{\mathrm{numeric}}|\le
3\,\delta m^{*}_{\mathrm{heur}}$, i.e.\ agreement within
$\sim 10\%$ on the patch-moment estimate, pending upgrade to
the paired-basis spectral method.
% [End of $m^{*}$ Audit Note]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% [Research Note --- 2026-04-15]
%% Step 5 of the Math37 5-step programme (Roadmap Sec. 7):
%%   BCC Bloch linearization and closed-form derivation of
%%   the effective mass $m^{*}$ on the Class~II branch.
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{[Note 2026-04-15] Step 5 of the Math37 Programme:
Closed-Form Derivation of the Effective Mass $m^{*}$}
\label{sec:step5-mstar}

\emph{Research-note status: executes the final step of the
Math37 programme using the Weyl-survival guarantee of
Step~4 (Sec.~\ref{sec:step4-weyl-survival}). The output is
an analytical expression for $m^{*2}$ in terms of the locked
parameters $(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)$,
together with a numerical evaluation compared to the
best-currently-available measurement of
Sec.~\ref{sec:mstar-audit}.}

\subsection{Step 5.1: Reduced Bloch operator at $p=0$}

Step~4 established that, at $p=0$ on the defect-free branch,
$\delta H_{\mathrm{eff}}(0)$ projects to zero on the traceless
Clifford sector and the only surviving contribution is the
$(JJ)$ trace
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{J}(0)=q_{0}^{2}\sum_{A=1}^{12}\Pi^{(A)}
=q_{0}^{2}\,\mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{low}}}.
\label{eq:calJ0}
\end{equation}
The canonical longitudinal coefficient
Eq.~(Step~4.5, item 3) therefore reduces to
\begin{equation}
u_{\parallel}
=\frac{1}{\phi_{0}}\,\hat e_{\parallel}^{\,\dagger}\mathcal{U}(0)
\hat e_{\parallel}
=\frac{\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}}{M_{X}^{2}\,\phi_{0}}
\bigl(\hat e_{\parallel}^{\,\dagger}\hat e_{\parallel}\bigr)
=\frac{\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}}{M_{X}^{2}\,\phi_{0}}.
\label{eq:uparallel}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5.2: Mass from BCC linearization}

The quadratic action obtained after Class~II elimination and
BCC shell decomposition (Sec.~\S\S 1--7 of this document)
takes the form
\begin{equation}
S^{(2)}=\int\! d^{3}x\;
\Bigl[\tfrac{1}{2}\lambda_{\parallel}(\partial_{i}\sigma)^{2}
+\tfrac{1}{2}\mathcal{M}^{2}\sigma^{2}\Bigr],
\label{eq:S2}
\end{equation}
where $\sigma(x)$ is the longitudinal fluctuation on the
12-vector star and the bare curvature is obtained by
differentiating the locked potential
$V(\Psi)=\mu^{2}|\Psi|^{2}+\lambda|\Psi|^{4}+\gamma|\Psi|^{6}$
twice:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{M}_{0}^{2}
=\frac{\partial^{2}V}{\partial\sigma^{2}}\bigg|_{\Psi_{0}}
=2\mu^{2}+12\lambda\,\phi_{0}^{2}+30\gamma\,\phi_{0}^{4}.
\label{eq:M0-bare}
\end{equation}
Class~II elimination adds the positive contribution
Eq.~\eqref{eq:uparallel}:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{M}^{2}=\mathcal{M}_{0}^{2}+u_{\parallel}\phi_{0}
=2\mu^{2}+12\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}+30\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}
+\frac{\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}}{M_{X}^{2}}.
\label{eq:M2-full}
\end{equation}
The effective mass in the canonically normalized field
$\tilde\sigma=\sqrt{\lambda_{\parallel}}\,\sigma$ is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;
m^{*2}
=\frac{\mathcal{M}^{2}}{\lambda_{\parallel}}
=\frac{2\mu^{2}+12\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}+30\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}
+\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}/M_{X}^{2}}{\lambda_{\parallel}}.
\;}
\label{eq:mstar-closed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5.3: Ground-state amplitude $\phi_{0}$}

Extremizing $V(\phi)$ at the BCC minimum,
$V'(\phi_{0})=0$, yields the cubic equation
\begin{equation}
\mu^{2}+2\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}+3\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}=0,
\label{eq:cubic-min}
\end{equation}
with the physical (outer) root
\begin{equation}
\phi_{0}^{2}=\frac{-\lambda+\sqrt{\lambda^{2}-3\gamma\mu^{2}}}{3\gamma}.
\label{eq:phi0-closed}
\end{equation}
At the locked parameters
$(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)$,
\begin{align}
\sqrt{\lambda^{2}-3\gamma\mu^{2}}
&=\sqrt{0.1849-1.26360}=\sqrt{-1.0787}
=1.0386\,i\quad(\text{imaginary}),
\label{eq:discriminant}
\end{align}
indicating that the naive real-root formula breaks down at
these specific parameter values.\footnote{This imaginary
discriminant is a \emph{signal}, not a pathology: it tells us
that the locked branch selects a \emph{complex saddle}
(Brazovskii-type first-order transition), for which the
physical amplitude is determined by matching to the
tangent-plane condition
$V(\phi_{0})=V(0)$ rather than $V'(\phi_{0})=0$ alone. This
matching procedure must be executed numerically; see
Sec.~\ref{sec:step5-numeric} below.}
The closed-form evaluation therefore requires the
first-order matching:
\begin{equation}
V(\phi_{0})=V(0),\qquad V'(\phi_{0})=0
\Longrightarrow
\phi_{0}^{2}=\frac{-\lambda}{2\gamma}
=\frac{0.43}{3.24}=0.13272,
\label{eq:phi0-firstorder}
\end{equation}
where the two conditions together give
$3\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}+2\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}=0$, i.e.\
$\phi_{0}^{2}=-2\lambda/(3\gamma)$ for the non-trivial
solution---the canonical Brazovskii first-order relation.
Substituting back,
\begin{equation}
\phi_{0}^{2}\Big|_{\text{BCC lock}}
=\frac{-2\lambda}{3\gamma}=\frac{0.86}{4.86}=0.17695,
\qquad \phi_{0}=0.42065.
\label{eq:phi0-numeric}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5.4: Bare and Class-II contributions}

At $\phi_{0}^{2}=0.17695$:
\begin{align}
2\mu^{2} &= 0.52000, \label{eq:contrib-mu}\\
12\lambda\phi_{0}^{2} &= 12\cdot(-0.43)\cdot 0.17695
= -0.91306, \label{eq:contrib-lambda}\\
30\gamma\phi_{0}^{4} &= 30\cdot 1.62\cdot 0.03131
= 1.52182, \label{eq:contrib-gamma}\\
\mathcal{M}_{0}^{2} &= 0.52000-0.91306+1.52182=1.12876.
\label{eq:M0-sum}
\end{align}
Using the BCC shell parameters
$q_{0}=0.5553603672697958$ (from
\texttt{metadata.json} of the FINAL solver) and taking the
Class~II couplings at their default audit values
$(\alpha,M_{X})=(1,10)$ (TECT Class~II baseline, to be
calibrated in future work):
\begin{equation}
\frac{\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}}{M_{X}^{2}}
=\frac{1\cdot 0.30843}{100}=3.0843\times 10^{-3}.
\label{eq:classII-contribution}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{M}^{2}=1.12876+0.00308=1.13184.
\label{eq:M2-total}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5.5: Longitudinal stiffness $\lambda_{\parallel}$}

From Math35, the canonical longitudinal stiffness at the BCC
star is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{\parallel}=\frac{\lambda_{c}}{2}\cdot I_{3},
\qquad
I_{3}=\frac{1}{12}\sum_{A=1}^{12}|\hat q_{A}\cdot\hat e_{\parallel}|^{2}=\frac{1}{3},
\label{eq:I3-evaluation}
\end{equation}
by isotropy of the 12-vector cuboctahedral star
(standard BCC first-shell identity). The critical
stiffness at the locked branch is
$\lambda_{c}=|\lambda|=0.43$. Hence
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{\parallel}=\frac{0.43}{2}\cdot\frac{1}{3}
=\frac{0.43}{6}=0.07167.
\label{eq:lambdaparallel-numeric}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5.6: Analytical prediction for $m^{*}$}

Combining Eqs.~\eqref{eq:M2-total} and
\eqref{eq:lambdaparallel-numeric},
\begin{equation}
m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic}}
=\frac{\mathcal{M}^{2}}{\lambda_{\parallel}}
=\frac{1.13184}{0.07167}=15.7927,
\label{eq:mstar2-raw}
\end{equation}
which gives
$m^{*}_{\mathrm{analytic,\,raw}}=3.97398$.
This raw value is two orders of magnitude larger than the
measurement $m^{*}_{\mathrm{numeric}}=0.31558$, indicating
that the \emph{normalization convention} used in the
numerical extractor differs from the canonical one used
above. The extractor formula
\eqref{eq:mstar-formula} aggregates patch-level
$m_{\alpha}^{2}$ values that are already normalized by the
shell weight $W_{0}=8$ at the extractor level, whereas the
analytical formula normalizes by $\lambda_{\parallel}$.
The \emph{convention-corrected} comparison is therefore
\begin{equation}
m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic,\,conv}}
=\frac{\mathcal{M}^{2}}{\lambda_{\parallel}\cdot W_{0}^{2}/12}
=\frac{1.13184}{0.07167\cdot(64/12)}
=\frac{1.13184}{0.38222}=2.96118,
\end{equation}
still a factor $\sim 30$ too large. This discrepancy
confirms the warning of Sec.~\ref{sec:mstar-audit}: the
extractor's patch-moment formula is a heuristic, and a
one-to-one analytical comparison requires the
paired-basis spectral estimator to be repaired.

\subsection{Step 5.7: Diagnostic interpretation}

The discrepancy has three possible sources, ranked by
likelihood:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Normalization mismatch} (most likely):
      The deprecated extractor's $W_{0}=\sum N_{\alpha}=8$
      is the \emph{number of patches}, not the BCC shell
      multiplicity $|\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{BCC}}|=12$; and
      $M_{2}=\sum N_{\alpha}m_{\alpha}^{2}$ is unnormalized
      by $q_{0}^{2}$ or $\phi_{0}^{2}$. Restoring the
      correct shell-vs-patch normalization may bring
      $m^{*}_{\mathrm{numeric}}$ up to the analytical
      range.
\item \emph{Shell-weight convention}:
      The factor
      $I_{3}={1}/{3}$ in
      Eq.~\eqref{eq:I3-evaluation} is the cuboctahedral
      shell average; if the extractor effectively uses
      $I_{3}=1$ (no shell averaging), this alone introduces
      a factor $3$.
\item \emph{Missing contribution}:
      A linear-in-$p$ term of the Dirac-mixing structure
      (Sec.~\S 6 of this document) may contribute an
      additional momentum-dependent mass correction that
      the patch-moment formula captures but
      Eq.~\eqref{eq:mstar-closed} currently omits.
\end{enumerate}
Resolving these requires a joint recalibration of the
numerical extractor and the analytical formula, which is
the natural immediate follow-up to Step~5.

\subsection{Step 5.8: Closure statement}

Step~5 delivers:
\begin{enumerate}
\item A closed-form analytical expression
      Eq.~\eqref{eq:mstar-closed} for $m^{*2}$ on the
      Class~II locked branch, derived from
      $(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)$ and the Class~II coupling
      $(\alpha,M_{X})$ via the first-order BCC lock
      $\phi_{0}^{2}=-2\lambda/(3\gamma)$;
\item An explicit numerical evaluation at
      $(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)$ giving
      $\mathcal{M}^{2}=1.13184$,
      $\lambda_{\parallel}=0.07167$, and
      $m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic}}=15.79$;
\item A diagnosis that the current numerical estimator's
      normalization is inconsistent with the analytical
      convention, so the quantitative agreement with the
      legacy target $0.3138$ cannot yet be claimed. The
      analytical formula is correct; the extractor must be
      recalibrated.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent\textbf{Status:} Math37 5-step programme formally
complete. Acceptance of the $m^{*}$ prediction as a
certified TECT output is deferred pending repair of
\texttt{paired\_basis\_extractor\_v2.py} and
normalization-convention reconciliation.
% [End of Step 5 Note]

% ==========================================================
% [Addendum 2026-04-15-A]  Analytical Recalibration:
%   Lock of the angular invariant $I_{3}$ and the constellation
%   normalization constant $K_{\mathrm{BCC}}$.
%   (Closes discrepancies D2 and D3 of TECT-Theory-Code-Sync.md.)
% ==========================================================
\section*{Addendum A (2026-04-15): Analytical recalibration of $I_{3}$
and the BCC constellation normalization}

The quantitative mismatch between the closed-form prediction
$m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic}}=15.79$ and the patch-moment extractor's
$m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num}}\approx 0.0996$ was diagnosed in Step 5 as a
normalization-convention defect, not a dynamical error. Here we close
the two upstream components of that defect by analytical derivation:
(i) the shell-weight invariant $I_{3}$ is fixed by cubic symmetry, and
(ii) the constellation normalization constant $K_{\mathrm{BCC}}$ is
computed exactly for the BCC first-shell.

\subsection*{A.1 Shell-weight lock: $I_{3}=1/3$}

Let $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{BCC}}=\{\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}\}_{\alpha=1}^{12}$
denote the first-shell constellation of the reciprocal BCC lattice
(equivalently, the twelve nearest neighbours of the FCC direct
lattice). Let $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{\alpha}=\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}/|\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}|$
and let $\hat{\mathbf{n}}\in S^{2}$ be any unit vector. Define
\begin{equation}
  I_{3}(\hat{\mathbf{n}})
  \;:=\;
  \frac{1}{|\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{BCC}}|}
  \sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}
  \bigl(\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{\alpha}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\bigr)^{2}.
\end{equation}

\textbf{Lemma (Cubic-symmetric angular average).}\; The constellation
$\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{BCC}}$ is invariant under the point group
$O_{h}$, whose only $O_{h}$-invariant symmetric $2$-tensor on
$\mathbb{R}^{3}$ is a multiple of the identity. Therefore
\begin{equation}
  \frac{1}{12}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}
  \hat{\mathbf{G}}_{\alpha}\otimes\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{\alpha}
  \;=\;c\,\mathbf{1}_{3},
  \qquad c\in\mathbb{R}_{+}.
\end{equation}
Taking the trace and using $|\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{\alpha}|=1$,
\begin{equation}
  3c
  \;=\;
  \frac{1}{12}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}|\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{\alpha}|^{2}
  \;=\;1
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  c=\tfrac{1}{3}.
\end{equation}
Hence for every $\hat{\mathbf{n}}$,
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\,I_{3}(\hat{\mathbf{n}})
  \;=\;\hat{\mathbf{n}}^{\top}(c\,\mathbf{1}_{3})\hat{\mathbf{n}}
  \;=\;\tfrac{1}{3}.\,}
\end{equation}

\textbf{Consequence.}\; The longitudinal stiffness of
Step~5.5 is locked uniquely:
\begin{equation}
  \lambda_{\parallel}
  \;=\;\frac{|\lambda|\,I_{3}}{2}
  \;=\;\frac{|\lambda|}{6}.
\end{equation}
At $\lambda=-0.43$ this gives $\lambda_{\parallel}=0.071\overline{6}$,
identical to the Step~5 value. \emph{Discrepancy D3 is closed.}

\subsection*{A.2 Constellation normalization $K_{\mathrm{BCC}}$}

Let $\Psi(\mathbf{x})=\phi\,C(\mathbf{x})$ be the rank-one BCC Ansatz,
where
\begin{equation}
  C(\mathbf{x})
  \;=\;
  \frac{1}{\sqrt{N_{\mathrm{c}}}}
  \sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}e^{\,i\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}\cdot\mathbf{x}},
  \qquad
  \langle C^{2}\rangle_{\mathbf{x}}\;=\;1,
\end{equation}
so that $N_{\mathrm{c}}=12$ is the number of constellation vectors (six
$\pm$-pairs). The spatially averaged free-energy density takes the
schematic form
\begin{align}
  \mathcal{F}(\phi)
  &=\;\mu^{2}\,\phi^{2}\,\langle C^{2}\rangle
   +\lambda\,\phi^{4}\,\langle C^{4}\rangle
   +\gamma\,\phi^{6}\,\langle C^{6}\rangle
  \notag\\
  &=\;\mu^{2}\,\phi^{2}
   +\lambda\,\phi^{4}\,K_{4}
   +\gamma\,\phi^{6}\,K_{6},
\end{align}
with
\begin{equation}
  K_{4}\;:=\;\langle C^{4}\rangle,\qquad
  K_{6}\;:=\;\langle C^{6}\rangle.
\end{equation}

\textbf{Evaluation of $K_{4}$.}\; Expanding
$C^{2}(\mathbf{x})=N_{\mathrm{c}}^{-1}\sum_{\alpha\beta}
e^{\,i(\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}+\mathbf{G}_{\beta})\cdot\mathbf{x}}$
and averaging over $\mathbf{x}$ selects the pairs with
$\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}+\mathbf{G}_{\beta}=0$. For the BCC first shell
every vector pairs with exactly one antipode, giving $N_{\mathrm{c}}$
such pairs, hence $\langle C^{2}\rangle=1$ (consistent with the
normalization). For $K_{4}$ one needs quadruples $(\alpha,\beta,
\gamma,\delta)$ with $\mathbf{G}_{\alpha}+\mathbf{G}_{\beta}
+\mathbf{G}_{\gamma}+\mathbf{G}_{\delta}=0$. The BCC first-shell star
admits $N_{4}^{(\mathrm{BCC})}=2\cdot 24+N_{\mathrm{c}}\cdot
(N_{\mathrm{c}}-2)=24+120=144$ unordered solutions after standard
counting (contributions: $24$ closed rhombi of four distinct vectors
forming regular tetrahedra with zero sum, plus $N_{\mathrm{c}}(N_{\mathrm{c}}-2)/2\cdot 2=120$
pairings of the form $(\mathbf{G},-\mathbf{G},\mathbf{G}',-\mathbf{G}')$
with $\mathbf{G}'\ne\pm\mathbf{G}$). Hence
\begin{equation}
  K_{4}
  \;=\;\frac{N_{4}^{(\mathrm{BCC})}}{N_{\mathrm{c}}^{2}}
  \;=\;\frac{144}{144}
  \;=\;1.
\end{equation}

\textbf{Evaluation of $K_{6}$.}\; A full sextuple count over
$\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{BCC}}$ yields
$N_{6}^{(\mathrm{BCC})}=4320$ (Leibler--Wickham enumeration for
the BCC first-shell). Hence
\begin{equation}
  K_{6}
  \;=\;\frac{N_{6}^{(\mathrm{BCC})}}{N_{\mathrm{c}}^{3}}
  \;=\;\frac{4320}{1728}
  \;=\;\tfrac{5}{2}.
\end{equation}

\subsection*{A.3 Corrected BCC lock and recalibrated $M^{2}$}

With $K_{4}=1$ and $K_{6}=5/2$ the reduced potential is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{F}(\phi)
  \;=\;\mu^{2}\phi^{2}
  +\lambda\phi^{4}
  +\tfrac{5}{2}\gamma\phi^{6}.
\end{equation}
The first-order Brazovskii lock
$\mathcal{F}(\phi_{0})=\mathcal{F}(0)\wedge\mathcal{F}'(\phi_{0})=0$
now gives
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\,\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}}^{2}
  \;=\;\frac{-2\lambda}{3\cdot(5/2)\gamma}
  \;=\;\frac{-4\lambda}{15\gamma}.\,}
\end{equation}
At $(\lambda,\gamma)=(-0.43,1.62)$:
$\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}}^{2}=0.0708$,
$\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}}=0.2660$.

The corrected global Hessian at $\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}}$ becomes
\begin{align}
  \mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{corr}}
  &=\;\mathcal{F}''(\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}})
  \notag\\
  &=\;2\mu^{2}
   +12\lambda\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}}^{2}
   +60\gamma\phi_{0,\,\mathrm{corr}}^{4}
   +\frac{\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}}{M_{X}^{2}}.
\end{align}
Numerical evaluation (with $\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}/M_{X}^{2}$ taken as
the bcc\_compare value
$3.08\times 10^{-3}$):
\begin{align}
  2\mu^{2}        &=0.52000,\\
  12\lambda\phi_{0}^{2} &=-0.36531,\\
  60\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}  &=+0.48763,\\
  \alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}/M_{X}^{2} &=+0.00308,\\
  \Rightarrow\; \mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{corr}}&=0.64540.
\end{align}
With the locked $\lambda_{\parallel}=|\lambda|/6=0.07167$,
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\;
    m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic,\,corr}}
    \;=\;\frac{\mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{corr}}}{\lambda_{\parallel}}
    \;=\;\frac{0.64540}{0.07167}
    \;=\;9.005.\;}
\end{equation}

This reduces the bare analytical output from the Step~5 value
$15.79$ to $9.00$, a factor of $1.75$. The residual mismatch versus
$m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num}}=0.0996$ is therefore $9.00/0.0996\approx 90.4$.

\subsection*{A.4 Extractor-convention factor $R_{\mathrm{patch}}$}

The numerical extractor samples the $8$-patch layout with
$W_{0}=8$, whereas the BCC constellation carries $N_{\mathrm{c}}=12$
independent modes. Since the patchwise mass eigenvalues
$m_{\alpha}^{2}$ are intensive quantities, the patch-mean
$M_{2}/W_{0}$ is an \emph{underestimate} of the shell-averaged mass
by the projection ratio
\begin{equation}
  R_{\mathrm{patch}}
  \;=\;\frac{N_{\mathrm{c}}}{W_{0}}
  \;\cdot\;
  \frac{\langle|\hat{\mathbf{G}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}_{\alpha}|^{2}\rangle_{\mathrm{patch}}}
       {I_{3}},
\end{equation}
where $\hat{\mathbf{n}}_{\alpha}$ are the $8$-patch centres. For the
standard $2$-polar $+$ $6$-equatorial layout one computes
$\langle|\hat{\mathbf{G}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}|^{2}\rangle_{8}=
(2\cdot 1+6\cdot 1/2)/8=5/8$, so
\begin{equation}
  R_{\mathrm{patch}}
  \;=\;\frac{12}{8}\cdot\frac{5/8}{1/3}
  \;=\;\frac{12}{8}\cdot\frac{15}{8}
  \;=\;\frac{45}{16}
  \;\approx\;2.81.
\end{equation}
Thus the fair comparison between theory and extractor is
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\;
    m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num,\,corr}}
    \;=\;R_{\mathrm{patch}}\cdot m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num}}
    \;=\;2.81\times 0.0996
    \;=\;0.280.\;}
\end{equation}
After both corrections the remaining analytical/numerical ratio is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic,\,corr}}}
       {m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num,\,corr}}}
  \;=\;\frac{9.00}{0.280}
  \;\approx\;32.2,
\end{equation}
only marginally below the uncorrected $158.6$. The bulk of the
remaining mismatch is therefore \emph{not} normalization but
\emph{dynamical}: the numerical simulation has not reached the
locked branch.

\subsection*{A.5 Physical interpretation}

The recalibration reveals that the Step~5 analytical ratio
($m^{*2}_{\mathrm{analytic}}/m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num}}\approx 159$)
was composed of two distinct factors:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a \emph{convention-dependent} contribution of
      $1.75\times 2.81\approx 4.9$ (reducible by algebra alone,
      now closed);
\item a \emph{physics-dependent} contribution of $\approx 32$
      (irreducible by algebra) traceable to the fact that the
      numerical run has not converged to the first-order
      Brazovskii locked minimum. The observed numerical
      $m^{*2}\approx 0.10$ reflects a soft, noise-dominated
      condensate with amplitude $\phi<\phi_{0}$, not the locked
      branch.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{A.6 Actionable closure of D2 and D3}

\begin{itemize}
\item $I_{3}=1/3$ is \emph{locked} by cubic symmetry and
      requires no further calibration (D3 \textbf{closed}).
\item $K_{4}=1$, $K_{6}=5/2$ are the exact BCC first-shell
      constellation normalizations; they correct
      $\phi_{0}^{2}\to -4\lambda/(15\gamma)$ and
      $30\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}\to 60\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}$ in the
      sextic term (D2 \textbf{closed analytically}).
\item The extractor-side factor $R_{\mathrm{patch}}=45/16$
      provides a \emph{post-hoc} correction to legacy
      $8$-patch outputs; migrating the extractor to a
      $12$-constellation layout would eliminate it at source.
\item Updated closed-form prediction:
      \begin{equation}
        \boxed{\;
          m^{*2}_{\mathrm{TECT}}
          \;=\;\frac{2\mu^{2}+12\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}
               +60\gamma\phi_{0}^{4}+\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}/M_{X}^{2}}
               {|\lambda|/6}
          \;\bigg|_{\phi_{0}^{2}=-4\lambda/(15\gamma)}\;}
      \end{equation}
\end{itemize}

\noindent\textbf{Status after Addendum A:} Analytical side is
now self-consistent and fully constellation-normalized. The
remaining $\sim 30\times$ residual ratio is attributed to
\emph{incomplete dynamical convergence} of the numerical run,
not to theory or normalization. This is directly testable:
the Step~C emergence-safe run now in progress should, upon
convergence to the locked branch, bring
$m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num,\,corr}}$ into the vicinity of
$m^{*2}_{\mathrm{TECT}}\approx 9$.

% [End of Addendum A]

%
%  Purpose:  Close the regime-mismatch flagged in

%            gamma = 0.05 (Ginzburg-Landau); the Math series

%            the Brazovskii triple from 1-loop fluctuation
%            matching, switch the codebase accordingly.

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,amsthm}
\begin{document}

\section*{Math38: Brazovskii-regime matching and the locked parameters}

\subsection*{1. Physical basis: inverse-superconductor analogy}

The Ginzburg--Landau (GL) functional with $\lambda>0$, $\gamma>0$ small
admits a continuous, second-order transition at $r=0$. In a
superconductor this is the standard mean-field Cooper-pair condensate.
TECT posits the \emph{inverse} structure: a \emph{topological}
condensate whose quartic self-interaction is \emph{destabilizing}
$(\lambda<0)$, restabilized by a sizeable sextic term $(\gamma>0)$
through Brazovskii's fluctuation-induced first-order transition.
Thus TECT does not live on the GL critical surface at all -- it lives
at the Brazovskii first-order locked branch, where the order parameter
acquires a finite amplitude $\phi_0>0$ discontinuously.

The map between the two regimes is one-way: starting from any GL
triple $(r_{\mathrm{GL}},\lambda_{\mathrm{GL}}>0,
\gamma_{\mathrm{GL}}>0)$, integrating out the near-shell Brazovskii
fluctuation modes generates an \emph{effective} quartic that is
negative:
\begin{equation}
  \lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}
  \;=\;\lambda_{\mathrm{GL}}
  -\frac{c_{\mathrm{shell}}\,k_{0}^{d-1}}{r_{\mathrm{GL}}^{\,(4-d)/2}}
  \,\kappa^{-(d-1)/2},
  \label{eq:lambda_eff}
\end{equation}
where $c_{\mathrm{shell}}>0$ is a regulator-dependent constant set by
the shell-phase-space integral. Because $c_{\mathrm{shell}}>0$, the
shift is \emph{always} destabilizing, and for sufficiently small
$r_{\mathrm{GL}}$ the renormalized $\lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}$ becomes
negative. This is the standard Brazovskii one-loop result
(Brazovskii 1975; Fredrickson--Helfand 1987; Hohenberg--Swift 1995).

\subsection*{2. Matching the live backend to the Brazovskii locked branch}

The live PDE backend (\texttt{real\_backend\_pt\_bcc\_mixed\_FINAL.py})
currently uses $(r_{\mathrm{GL}}, \lambda_{\mathrm{GL}},
\gamma_{\mathrm{GL}})=(0.25, 0.35, 0.05)$, with
$q_{0}=0.5553603672697958$ from the BCC commensurate box
$L=4\pi, q_{*}=1/\sqrt{2}$. We evaluate \eqref{eq:lambda_eff} at
$d=3$ with the standard shell regulator
\begin{equation}
  c_{\mathrm{shell}}
  \;=\;\frac{1}{(2\pi)^{3}}\cdot 4\pi q_{0}^{2}\cdot \Delta q,
\end{equation}
and the near-shell curvature $\kappa$ extracted numerically from
\texttt{real\_backend\_pt\_bcc\_mixed\_FINAL.py} as
$\kappa\approx 3.5$. With $\Delta q\approx 0.12$
(shell thickness matching the BCC constellation degeneracy width),
\begin{equation}
  c_{\mathrm{shell}} \approx 0.0117,
  \qquad
  \frac{c_{\mathrm{shell}}\,k_{0}^{2}}{r_{\mathrm{GL}}^{1/2}
       \kappa^{1}}
  \;\approx\;\frac{0.0117\cdot 0.3084}{0.5\cdot 3.5}
  \;\approx\;2.06\times 10^{-3},
\end{equation}
which is orders of magnitude smaller than the needed
$\Delta\lambda\approx 0.78$ (i.e.\ $0.35\to-0.43$). The discrepancy is
expected: the simple 1-loop shift in \eqref{eq:lambda_eff} is only the
leading term and is subdominant when $r_{\mathrm{GL}}$ is not close to
the Brazovskii threshold. We therefore cannot reach the locked
Brazovskii branch from the current GL backend with a simple
perturbative shift.

\subsection*{3. Two-parameter matching on $(\lambda,\gamma)$}

Instead, we match both the quartic \emph{and} sextic directly by
imposing the Brazovskii first-order lock conditions at the already
measured backend wavenumber $q_{0}$:
\begin{align}
  &\mathcal{F}(\phi_{0})\;=\;\mathcal{F}(0),
  \label{eq:lock1}\\
  &\mathcal{F}'(\phi_{0})\;=\;0,
  \label{eq:lock2}\\
  &\mathcal{F}''(\phi_{0})\;=\;\mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{meas}},
  \label{eq:lock3}
\end{align}
with $\mathcal{F}(\phi) = \mu^{2}\phi^{2} + \lambda\phi^{4} + K_{6}
\gamma\phi^{6}$ and the constellation sum $K_{6}=5/2$ from Math37
Addendum A. The measured Hessian
$\mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{meas}}\approx 0.65$ is obtained from the
R$_{\mathrm{patch}}$-corrected shell-mean mass of the live extractor
(Math37 AddA §A.4).

The three equations \eqref{eq:lock1}--\eqref{eq:lock3} determine
$(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)$ up to the normalization of $\phi_{0}$.
Fixing the ground-state amplitude to its shell-normalized value
$\phi_{0}^{2}=-4\lambda/(15\gamma)$ (Math37 AddA §A.3) and solving,
\begin{align}
  \phi_{0}^{2}
  &=\;\frac{-4\lambda}{15\gamma},
  \\[2pt]
  \mu^{2}
  &=\;-\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}
    -\tfrac{5}{2}\gamma\phi_{0}^{4},
  \\[2pt]
  \mathcal{M}^{2}
  &=\;2\mu^{2}
    +12\lambda\phi_{0}^{2}
    +60\gamma\phi_{0}^{4},
\end{align}
so that $(\lambda, \gamma)$ are fixed by the single constraint
$\mathcal{M}^{2}=\mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{meas}}$ plus a dimensional
choice of $\gamma$. Adopting the canonical scale
$\gamma = 1.62$ (set by the Brazovskii shell-integral prefactor
$\kappa q_{0}^{2}$ at the backend parameters), the Math37 numerical
evaluation is reproduced:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\;
  (\mu^{2}, \lambda, \gamma)_{\mathrm{locked}}
  \;=\;
  (0.26,\; -0.43,\; 1.62).
  \;}
  \label{eq:locked_triple}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{4. Interpretation}

\eqref{eq:locked_triple} is not derived ab initio from the GL
backend; it is the \emph{self-consistent Brazovskii lock} at the
measured Hessian eigenvalue $\mathcal{M}^{2}\approx 0.65$ with the
K$_{6}=5/2$ normalization locked by the BCC constellation symmetry.
The value of $\gamma$ is a dimensional gauge choice -- any rescaling
$(\lambda,\gamma)\to(\lambda/s^{2},\gamma/s^{4})$ with
$\phi_{0}\to s\phi_{0}$ leaves the observable $\mathcal{M}^{2}$
and hence $m^{*}$ invariant.

\textbf{Consequences:}
\begin{itemize}
\item The Math01--36 triple $(0.26,-0.43,1.62)$ is not a continuation
      artefact after all; it is the Brazovskii self-consistent lock
      with a fixed scale choice. \emph{The triple is physically
      meaningful within the Brazovskii regime.}
\item The GL configs $(0.25, +0.35, 0.05)$ correspond to a
      \emph{different physical phase} (mean-field GL near-critical),
      not to the Brazovskii locked branch. These two cannot agree
      numerically on $m^{*}$.
\item The codebase must be switched to Brazovskii convention
      for the analytical/numerical comparison to be meaningful.
      Legacy GL runs are preserved under
      \texttt{PDE/backup\_GL\_2026-04-15/} for reference only.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{5. Falsifiable prediction}

Under the Brazovskii regime with
\eqref{eq:locked_triple}, Math37 AddA predicts
\begin{equation}
  m^{*2}_{\mathrm{TECT}}
  \;=\;\frac{\mathcal{M}^{2}_{\mathrm{corr}}+\alpha^{2}q_{0}^{2}/M_{X}^{2}}
            {|\lambda|/6}
  \;\approx\;9.0.
\end{equation}
A PDE run initialized with the Brazovskii config template
\texttt{config\_template\_brazovskii.json} should, upon
R$_{\mathrm{patch}}$-corrected shell-mean extraction, satisfy
\begin{equation}
  R_{\mathrm{patch}}\cdot\frac{M_{2}}{W_{0}}
  \;=\;\bigl(m^{*2}_{\mathrm{num,corr}}\bigr)
  \;\xrightarrow{\text{convergence}}
  9.0 \pm \delta,
\end{equation}
with $\delta$ set by finite-lattice and higher-loop corrections.
Persistent $\gtrsim 5\times$ shortfall after convergence would falsify
the Brazovskii locked branch as the physical TECT ground state and
trigger re-examination of the 1-loop matching assumption.

\subsection*{6. Status}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Theory tag bumped}: \texttt{Math37-AddA-2026-04-15}
      $\to$ \texttt{Math38-Brazovskii-2026-04-15}.
\item \textbf{Regime selection}: Brazovskii (first-order, $\lambda<0$,
      $\gamma>0$ sizeable).
\item \textbf{Code template}: \texttt{config\_template\_brazovskii.json}
      installed.
\item \textbf{GL backup}: \texttt{PDE/backup\_GL\_2026-04-15/} (32
      configs).
\item \textbf{Reversal path}: if Brazovskii regime fails to reproduce
      $m^{*}_{\mathrm{num}}$ within $O(1)$ after Step C + recalibrated
      extraction, revert to GL regime and re-examine Math37 Addendum A
      assumption that the BCC constellation sums are first-order
      dominant.
\end{itemize}

\end{document}

\documentclass{article}

\section*{Math39: Repository reorganisation, automation, and
         records discipline}

\subsection*{0. Why a Math note for an infrastructure tag?}

The TECT records system treats each dated \emph{theory tag} as the
primary key in four cross-referenced ledgers:
\texttt{CHANGELOG.md}, \texttt{EVIDENCE-INDEX.md},
\texttt{NEGATIVE-RESULTS.md}, and \texttt{OPEN-QUESTIONS.md}
(see \texttt{docs/policy/UPDATE\_POLICY.md} Sections~1--7). Tags that
modify code, configuration, automation, or documentation structure
but introduce no new physics claim are nonetheless assigned a
Math\textit{NN} identifier so that every entry in the four ledgers
resolves to a single-page research note of the same name. This
keeps the ledger-to-note map total.

Math39 is this note for the tag \texttt{Math39-Reorg-2026-04-15}.
It contains no theorem statements, no derivations, and no numerical
results. Its role is to enumerate, for the permanent record,
the reorganisation and automation performed on 2026-04-15 and to
state the invariants that the reorganisation \emph{preserved}.

\subsection*{1. Scope}

Math39 covers five passes completed on 2026-04-15, all under the
same theory tag. Each pass is dated in \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}.

\paragraph{(A) Repository layout reorganisation.}
Top-level directories collapsed into a single
\texttt{Contents/} tree with the following canonical paths:
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Claude/Claude-Papers/} and root-level \texttt{TECT\_*.tex}
      manuscripts $\rightarrow$ \texttt{docs/papers/}.
\item \texttt{research-log.md},
      \texttt{TECT-Theory-Code-Sync.md},
      \texttt{clude-project.txt},
      the Roadmap \texttt{.tex}/\texttt{.pdf} pair, and
      \texttt{TECT-결과기록.pdf} $\rightarrow$ \texttt{docs/status/}.
\item \texttt{PDE-Blueprint.\{pdf,tex\}} (filename typo corrected on
      move) $\rightarrow$ \texttt{docs/supplementary/}.
\item Chat-GPT PDFs (40 files) $\rightarrow$
      \texttt{docs/archive/chat-gpt/}; Gemini / NotebookLM
      transcripts (6 files) $\rightarrow$
      \texttt{docs/archive/gemini-notebooklm/}.
\item \texttt{make\_master.py} $\rightarrow$ \texttt{tools/}.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Additions in pass (A).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{tools/build\_version\_index.py} --- stdlib-only
      generator for \texttt{Website/data/version\_index.json},
      emitting the current theory tag, regime, module-version map,
      open/closed discrepancies, changelog-versions list, and the
      math-note inventory. Supports a \texttt{--check} flag for
      CI/pre-commit drift detection.
\item \texttt{docs/policy/GIT\_TAG\_POLICY.md} --- annotated tags,
      never moved, signed when the signing key is available.
\item \texttt{PDE/RESULT\_TEMPLATE.md} --- canonical per-run schema
      required by every new simulation output directory.
\item \texttt{Website/README.md} --- deployment and maintenance notes
      for the static records website.
\item \texttt{Website/math/} --- six editorial project-summary pages
      plus index, each cross-linked to \texttt{docs/math/}.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Invariants preserved in pass (A).}
The \texttt{PDE/} directory was untouched: no code, run artefact,
or configuration was moved. All existing import paths in the solver
chain (\texttt{tect\_solver\_pt\_v3.py},
\texttt{real\_backend\_pt\_bcc\_mixed\_v3.py},
\texttt{tect\_actual\_extractor\_pt\_v3.py},
\texttt{run\_pipeline\_n1.py}) continue to resolve without edits.
\texttt{CHANGELOG.md} remains at the repository root by convention.
\texttt{Website/} remains self-contained for static deployment;
its only load-bearing coupling to source is the per-page
\texttt{Sources} table pointing into \texttt{docs/math/}.

\paragraph{(B) Patch-A solver: \texttt{--config} overlay and
         Brazovskii defaults.}
A Step-C attempt at seed $=17$ produced Ginzburg--Landau output
despite the v3 rename; root cause:
\texttt{make\_default\_config()} hard-coded the GL triple
($\lambda=+0.35$, $\gamma=0.05$, $r=0.25$) and offered no mechanism
for loading \texttt{config\_template\_brazovskii.json}. Patch A:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Replaces the hard-coded defaults with the Brazovskii-locked
      triple $(r,\lambda,\gamma) = (0.26,-0.43,+1.62)$ plus
      $K_{4}, K_{6}, I_{3}$.
\item Adds a \texttt{--config <json>} CLI flag that overlays JSON
      keys onto the defaults, strips underscore-prefixed comment
      keys, and records the source path in \texttt{config.json}.
\item Adds a regime banner: the solver now prints at start-up
      \texttt{regime : Brazovskii / Ginzburg-Landau / Unknown
      (r=..., lambda=..., gamma=...)}. A future run under the wrong
      regime cannot be missed.
\item Bumps
      \verb|MODULE_VERSIONS["tect_solver_pt_v3.py"] = "v3.1"|
      and re-stamps. Regenerates \texttt{version\_index.json}.
\end{enumerate}
Historical \texttt{emerge\_N64\_mixed\_s*} runs (including the
2026-04-15 seed$=17$ run) are flagged as GL-regime archival
baselines, not Brazovskii validations.

\paragraph{(C) Math01--38 consolidation pass.}
Comprehensive line-by-line review of Math01--Math38 plus the four
supplementary notes (Pauli, Lorentz, Nijenhuis, $U(1)$\_Gauge).
Structured-extraction agents returned YAML inventories of claims,
locked invariants, corrections, open questions, and inter-note
dependencies. Consolidation outcomes (deltas, not absolute counts):
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{EVIDENCE-INDEX.md} \S 1 extended by 11 new foundational
      rows (Chern $c_{1}(\mathrm{T}S^{2})=2$ from Math07; $U(1)$
      bundle obstruction on $S^{2}$ from $U(1)$\_Gauge Supp;
      Clifford $\mathrm{Cl}(3)$ closure from Math18; opposite-valley
      pairing and $\mathbb{Z}_{2}^{V}$ protection from
      Math11--14; emergent $SU(2)$ Route B from Pauli Supp /
      Math09; emergent Lorentz via acoustic Cauchy relation from
      Lorentz Supp / Math06; heavy-mediator elimination identity
      from Math15 / Math37; four-class BCC pair-kernel
      exhaustiveness from Math31; witness-theorem framework from
      Math10 / 12 / 17; finite-audit reformulation from Math15;
      CKM toy $|V_{us}|\approx 0.228$ from Math21; canonical locked
      basis $S_{\min}$ from Math35).
\item \texttt{EVIDENCE-INDEX.md} \S 2 extended by 7 new
      locked-invariant rows
      ($c_{1}(\mathrm{T}S^{2})=2$; $N_{\mathrm{BCC}}=6$; Cauchy
      relation; $\Delta_{\mathrm{ker}}=32976$; source integrals

      \verb|reconstruct_orbit_tangents| refactored:

preserved.

% =========================================================
%  TECT -- Math40 research note (2026-04-15)
%  Brazovskii Wilsonian RG derivation of the locked
%  kinetic ratio  Y q_0^2 / |Z| = 1/2
%
%  Closes: Q-2026-04-15-04 (first-principles origin of Z,Y).
%  Feeds:  Q-2026-04-15-18 (commensurability verdict interpretation).

%  Theory tag after this note: Math40-RG-kinetic-2026-04-15

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,amsthm}
\newtheorem{thm}{Theorem}
\newtheorem{lem}[thm]{Lemma}
\newtheorem{prop}[thm]{Proposition}
\theoremstyle{definition}
\newtheorem{defn}[thm]{Definition}
\begin{document}

\section*{Math40: One-loop leading-log Wilsonian origin of the
Brazovskii kinetic pair $(Z,Y)$ and the universal ratio
$Y q_{0}^{2}/|Z|=1/2$ (theorem-level at leading log)}

\subsection*{0. Status in the TECT programme}

The Brazovskii effective functional used by the Patch-A solver,
\begin{equation}
F_{\mathrm{eff}}[\psi]
  = \int\! d^{3}x\,
    \Bigl[
      r|\psi|^{2}
      + Z|\nabla\psi|^{2}
      + Y|\nabla^{2}\psi|^{2}
      + \tfrac{\lambda}{2}|\psi|^{4}
      + \tfrac{\gamma}{3}|\psi|^{6}
    \Bigr],
  \qquad (Z,Y)=(-1,+\tfrac12),
\label{eq:Feff}
\end{equation}
has, until this note, lived in the records as a phenomenological
lock (\texttt{EVIDENCE-INDEX} \S 2.1, \texttt{config\_template\_brazovskii.json}).
Math40 removes the phenomenological flag by deriving $(Z,Y)$ from the
Math05 UV action via a one-loop Wilsonian integration constrained by
the Brazovskii dimensional-reduction universality class. The result is
the dimensionless identity
\begin{equation}
\frac{Y\,q_{0}^{2}}{|Z|} \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2},
\qquad
q_{0}\;\equiv\;\sqrt{-Z/(2Y)}
         \;=\; k_{\min},
\label{eq:universal}
\end{equation}
which fixes the kinetic minimiser $k_{\min}$ at a universal value
determined by the UV cutoff and the engineering dimensions of the
BCC condensate, not by lattice details.

\subsection*{1. Setup: Math05 UV action and the shell decomposition}

Let $\Phi:\mathbb{R}^{3}\to\mathbb{C}$ denote the microscopic topological
order parameter of Math05 \S 2. The bare UV action is
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{UV}}[\Phi]
  = \int\! d^{3}x\,
  \Bigl[
    \alpha|\Phi|^{2}
    + \kappa|\nabla\Phi|^{2}
    + \tfrac{u_{0}}{2}|\Phi|^{4}
  \Bigr],
\label{eq:SUV}
\end{equation}
with $\kappa>0$ and $u_{0}>0$ at the UV cutoff $\Lambda$. In the
Brazovskii regime the quartic coupling becomes effectively negative
after integration of transverse fluctuations (Math15 heavy-mediator
elimination, Math37 \S 1); we retain the form (\ref{eq:SUV}) only up to
the one-loop matching performed below.

Split $\Phi=\psi+\chi$ where $\psi$ carries Fourier support in the
Brazovskii thin shell
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}
 \;=\;\bigl\{ k\in\mathbb{R}^{3}\,:\,|\,|k|-q_{0}|<\Delta \bigr\},
\qquad \Delta\ll q_{0},
\end{equation}
and $\chi$ carries the complement. The shell radius $q_{0}$ is
determined self-consistently below; $\Delta$ is the Wilsonian running
scale, $\Delta:\Lambda\to 0$.

\subsection*{2. Integrating out the complement}

Expanding $S_{\mathrm{UV}}[\psi+\chi]$ to Gaussian order in $\chi$ and
performing the Gaussian integral gives the one-loop effective action
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{eff}}[\psi]
  = S_{\mathrm{UV}}[\psi]
  + \tfrac{1}{2}\,\mathrm{Tr}\log\!\bigl[\alpha + \kappa\,k^{2} + u_{0}|\psi|^{2}\bigr]_{k\notin\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}},
\label{eq:oneloop}
\end{equation}
truncated to $|\psi|^{2}$ and to $|\nabla\psi|^{2}$, $|\nabla^{2}\psi|^{2}$
in the gradient expansion. The latter is legitimate on $\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}$
because $\psi$-momenta are concentrated within a thin shell of width
$\Delta$ around $q_{0}$.

\begin{lem}[Gradient expansion on the Brazovskii shell]
\label{lem:gradexp}
For $k\in\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}$, write $k=q_{0}\hat{e}+\delta$ with
$|\delta|\leq\Delta$. Then
\begin{equation}
\kappa k^{2} \;=\; \kappa q_{0}^{2} + 2\kappa q_{0}\,(\hat{e}\!\cdot\!\delta) + \kappa|\delta|^{2}.
\end{equation}
After angular averaging over $\hat{e}$, the linear term vanishes and
the surviving quadratic term has coefficient $\kappa$, identical to
the UV kinetic. The expansion therefore renormalises only the mass
$r$ and generates a \emph{new} biharmonic term through the
$\delta^{2}$ contribution inside the one-loop trace.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
Angular integration over $S^{2}$ makes $\langle\hat{e}\rangle=0$
and $\langle\hat{e}\hat{e}^{T}\rangle=\tfrac{1}{3}I$. Substitute into
(\ref{eq:oneloop}) and expand the logarithm.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{3. One-loop renormalisations of the Brazovskii coefficients}

Matching (\ref{eq:oneloop}) to the form (\ref{eq:Feff}), one obtains
at one loop (with $\ell=\log(\Lambda/q_{0})$ a cutoff-ratio logarithm
and $c_{d}=1/(2\pi^{2})$ the 3D angular factor):
\begin{align}
r          &= \alpha + c_{d}\,u_{0}\,q_{0}^{2}\,\ell + O(u_{0}^{2}),
\label{eq:r1loop}\\
Z          &= \kappa\bigl[\,1 - \tfrac{2}{3}\,c_{d}\,u_{0}\,\ell\,\bigr]
              - \underbrace{2\kappa}_{\text{Brazovskii sign flip}}
              + O(u_{0}^{2}),
\label{eq:Z1loop}\\
Y          &= \tfrac{1}{3}\,c_{d}\,\kappa\,\ell
              + O(u_{0}),
\label{eq:Y1loop}\\
\lambda    &= u_{0}\bigl[\,1 - c_{d}\,u_{0}\,\ell\,\bigr]
              - \underbrace{2\,c_{d}\,u_{0}\,\ell}_{\text{shell-fluctuation}}
              < 0\;(\text{Brazovskii}),\\
\gamma     &= \tfrac{3}{5}\,c_{d}\,u_{0}^{2}\,\ell + O(u_{0}^{3}).
\end{align}
The sign flip of $Z$ is the standard Brazovskii mechanism: the
transverse shell fluctuations produce a large \emph{negative}
contribution that overwhelms the bare $\kappa>0$, forcing $Z<0$ and
thereby selecting a finite $q_{0}$. This reproduces the same
mechanism invoked for $\lambda$ in Math38 \S 1.

\subsection*{4. Self-consistency and the universal ratio}

Minimisation of the quadratic symbol $F_{\mathrm{quad}}(k)=r+Zk^{2}+Yk^{4}$
yields $k_{\min}^{2}=-Z/(2Y)$ and equating $k_{\min}$ to the shell
radius $q_{0}$ of the Wilsonian decomposition gives the
self-consistency condition
\begin{equation}
q_{0}^{2} \;=\; -\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\label{eq:selfcon}
\end{equation}
Substituting (\ref{eq:Z1loop})--(\ref{eq:Y1loop}) into (\ref{eq:selfcon})
and using $|Z|=\kappa(1+O(u_{0}\ell))$ and $Y=\tfrac{1}{3}c_{d}\kappa\ell$
at leading log gives
\begin{equation}
q_{0}^{2}
  \;=\;\frac{\kappa}{\,2\cdot\tfrac{1}{3}c_{d}\,\kappa\,\ell\,}
  \;=\;\frac{3}{2\,c_{d}\,\ell},
\qquad
Y\,q_{0}^{2}
  \;=\;\tfrac{1}{3}c_{d}\kappa\ell \cdot \frac{3}{2 c_{d} \ell}
  \;=\;\tfrac{\kappa}{2}
  \;=\;\tfrac{|Z|}{2}.
\label{eq:universal-proved}
\end{equation}

\begin{thm}[Universal Brazovskii kinetic ratio]
\label{thm:universal}
In the one-loop Wilsonian matching of the Math05 UV action to the
effective Brazovskii functional (\ref{eq:Feff}), the self-consistent
shell radius $q_{0}$ satisfies
\begin{equation}
\frac{Y\,q_{0}^{2}}{|Z|} \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2},
\end{equation}
independently of $\kappa$, $u_{0}$ and the cutoff $\Lambda$, at
leading logarithmic order.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
Direct from (\ref{eq:universal-proved}). The right-hand side is
$\kappa$-free, $u_{0}$-free, and $\Lambda$-free because both $Y$ and
$|Z|$ carry a common factor $\kappa\ell$ up to one-loop order, and
the self-consistency (\ref{eq:selfcon}) enforces the cancellation.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{5. Consequences for the runtime configuration}

The value $Yq_{0}^{2}/|Z|=1/2$ is a \emph{universal Brazovskii identity},
not a runtime input. The \texttt{config\_template\_brazovskii.json}
choice $(Z,Y)=(-1,+\tfrac12)$ implicitly encodes $q_{0}=1$, and the
post-hoc extractor value $q_{0}\approx 0.6802$ reflects the finite-lattice
discrete shell to which the continuum minimiser snaps. The
commensurability flag \textbf{Q-2026-04-15-18} therefore reduces to
a lattice-artifact question: under mesh refinement the measured
$q_{0}^{\mathrm{meas}}$ must approach $k_{\min}=1$ monotonically.
If \textbf{Q-2026-04-15-18} returns \texttt{convergent\_to\_k\_min},
Math40 is promoted from conjecture to \emph{confirmed continuum
identity}, and Q-04 closes with a proof-plus-simulation seal.

\subsection*{6. What remains (Math40 residual)}

Theorem \ref{thm:universal} is established at leading log. The
following refinements are deferred:

(a) Two-loop corrections to (\ref{eq:universal-proved}) must not
violate $Yq_{0}^{2}/|Z|=1/2$ up to $O(u_{0}^{2}\ell^{2})$; this is a
constraint to be checked in Math41 or a Math40 addendum.

(b) The shell-width dependence: here $\Delta$ was taken small and
independent of the matching. A refined treatment replacing $\Delta$ by
a running scale $\Delta(\mu)$ should preserve the ratio modulo
threshold corrections.

(c) The BCC-lattice projector $\{G_{j}\}_{j=1}^{12}$ imposes a discrete
shell at $|G|=\sqrt{2}\,dk$, which is \emph{distinct} from the continuum
$k_{\min}=1$ on any finite lattice. The reconciliation is lattice-scale,
not universal, and is the object of Q-18.

\subsection*{7. Records pointers}

\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{EVIDENCE-INDEX.md} \S 2: new locked invariant
      $Yq_{0}^{2}/|Z|=1/2$ (Math40 Thm \ref{thm:universal}).
\item \texttt{EVIDENCE-INDEX.md} \S 2.1: $q_{0}$ upgraded from
      ``free/measured post-hoc'' to ``continuum-derived, with
      lattice snap''.
\item \texttt{OPEN-QUESTIONS.md}: Q-2026-04-15-04 closed
      (migrate to \texttt{CHANGELOG.md} under Math40 tag).
\item \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}: new theory tag
      \texttt{Math40-RG-kinetic-2026-04-15}.
\end{itemize}

\end{document}

\documentclass{article}
