% =========================================================
%  TECT -- Math46b research note (2026-04-16)
%  Probe-mode linear-response definition of the Math44
%  Yang-Mills kinetic coefficients (c_W, c_B).
%
%  Purpose:
%    The Math46 v0.1 C3 extractor falsely attempted to read c_W, c_B
%    from vacuum averages <F^2>, <B^2> at the locked background.
%    That is wrong: on the Brazovskii-locked vacuum the gauge
%    sector is flat (F_mn = 0, B_mn = 0 up to lattice noise), so
%    any vacuum expectation of F^2 / B^2 is noise, NOT the
%    coupling constant.
%
%    Math46b fixes this by defining c_W, c_B as the second
%    functional derivatives of the effective action with respect
%    to prescribed probe gauge fluctuations, and by supplying the
%    extraction identities that a faithful C3 extractor must
%    implement.
%
%  Feeds: Math46 §3 (C3 extractor redesign);
%         Math44 Thm cWcB (closure).
%
%  Theory tag after this note: Math46b-probe-response-2026-04-16
% =========================================================

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,amsthm}
\newtheorem{thm}{Theorem}
\newtheorem{lem}[thm]{Lemma}
\newtheorem{prop}[thm]{Proposition}
\newtheorem{cor}[thm]{Corollary}
\theoremstyle{definition}
\newtheorem{defn}[thm]{Definition}
\theoremstyle{remark}
\newtheorem*{rmk}{Remark}
\begin{document}

\section*{Math46b: Probe-mode linear-response definition of the
Math44 Yang--Mills kinetic coefficients $(c_{W},c_{B})$}

\subsection*{0. Motivation}

On the Brazovskii-locked Class-III vacuum, the emergent gauge
connection $A_{\mu}^{(0)}(x) = -iF_{0}^{\dagger}(x)\partial_{\mu}F_{0}(x)$
is pure gauge: its curvature
$\mathcal{F}_{\mu\nu}^{(0)}=0$ up to $O(dx^{2})$ lattice noise.
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\bigl\langle F^{a}_{\mu\nu}F^{a,\mu\nu}\bigr\rangle_{\mathrm{vac}}
\;=\;0,
\qquad
\bigl\langle B_{\mu\nu}B^{\mu\nu}\bigr\rangle_{\mathrm{vac}}
\;=\;0,
\label{eq:vac-trivial}
\end{equation}
so the $c_{W},c_{B}$ appearing in Math44 Thm~cWcB \emph{cannot} be
read off a vacuum expectation. They are kinetic coefficients of a
functional that appears only \emph{once a source is applied}. The
correct definition is linear-response.

\subsection*{1. Linear-response definition of $(c_{W},c_{B})$}

\begin{defn}[Effective action on a gauge-perturbed background]
\label{defn:Seff-source}
Let $F_{0}(x)$ denote the locked frame of Math44 Lem (frame
completion). Let $a_{\mu}(x)\in\mathfrak{u}(2)$ be a prescribed
external source, decomposed as
\begin{equation}
a_{\mu}(x) \;=\; w_{\mu}^{a}(x)\,T^{a}\;+\;b_{\mu}(x)\,Y.
\label{eq:amu-def}
\end{equation}
Deform the frame by a left-action:
\begin{equation}
F_{a}(x) \;:=\; F_{0}(x)\,\mathrm{Pexp}\!\left[i\int_{x_{0}}^{x}\!
a_{\mu}(y)\,dy^{\mu}\right].
\label{eq:Fa-def}
\end{equation}
Define the one-loop effective action in the fast-mode integration
of Math44 \S 4:
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a]
 \;:=\;\tfrac{1}{2}\,\mathrm{Tr}\log\bigl[-D_{a}^{2}+U''(\rho_{D})\bigr]
 \Bigm|_{\mathrm{shell}\,\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}},
\qquad
D_{a,\mu}\;=\;\partial_{\mu}-iA_{\mu}^{(0)}-ia_{\mu}.
\label{eq:Seff-def}
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[Probe-response coefficients]
\label{defn:cWcB}
The Yang--Mills kinetic coefficients are the second functional
derivatives of $S_{\mathrm{eff}}$ with respect to the source at
$a=0$:
\begin{align}
c_{W}\,\delta^{ab}\,(\delta_{\mu\rho}\delta_{\nu\sigma}
   - \delta_{\mu\sigma}\delta_{\nu\rho})
  &\;\equiv\;
  \frac{1}{V}\,\frac{\delta^{2}S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a]}
    {\delta f^{a}_{\mu\nu}(x)\,\delta f^{b}_{\rho\sigma}(y)}
  \Bigg|_{a=0}
  \,,\label{eq:cW-def}\\[2pt]
c_{B}\,(\delta_{\mu\rho}\delta_{\nu\sigma}
   - \delta_{\mu\sigma}\delta_{\nu\rho})
  &\;\equiv\;
  \frac{1}{V}\,\frac{\delta^{2}S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a]}
    {\delta g_{\mu\nu}(x)\,\delta g_{\rho\sigma}(y)}
  \Bigg|_{a=0}
  \,,\label{eq:cB-def}
\end{align}
where $f^{a}_{\mu\nu}:=\partial_{\mu}w_{\nu}^{a}-\partial_{\nu}w_{\mu}^{a}$
and $g_{\mu\nu}:=\partial_{\mu}b_{\nu}-\partial_{\nu}b_{\mu}$ are
the \emph{linearised} field strengths (the non-Abelian commutator
term $-i[a_{\mu},a_{\nu}]$ drops out at second order). The factor
$V=N^{3}(dx)^{3}$ normalises to the intensive coefficient.
\end{defn}

\begin{rmk}
Definition (\ref{eq:cW-def})--(\ref{eq:cB-def}) is the correct
operational replacement for Math46 v0.1's mistaken vacuum averages.
$c_{W},c_{B}$ are \emph{response functions}, not order parameters.
\end{rmk}

\subsection*{2. Plane-wave probe identities}

\begin{lem}[Plane-wave response]
\label{lem:plane-wave}
Let the source be a single-mode probe
\begin{equation}
a_{\mu}(x)\;=\;\varepsilon\,\bigl[\,
  \hat{e}^{a}_{\mu}T^{a}\,+\,\hat{e}^{0}_{\mu}Y
\,\bigr]\,\cos(q\!\cdot\!x),
\qquad
\varepsilon \ll 1,
\end{equation}
with $\hat{e}^{a}_{\mu}\,q^{\mu}=0$ (transverse polarisation) and
$|q|\ll q_{0}$. Then
\begin{equation}
\Delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}(\varepsilon,q)
 \;:=\; S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a]\,-\,S_{\mathrm{eff}}[0]
 \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,V\,\varepsilon^{2}\,q^{2}\,
   \Bigl[
     c_{W}\,\hat{e}^{a}_{\mu}\hat{e}^{a,\mu}
     \,+\,c_{B}\,\hat{e}^{0}_{\mu}\hat{e}^{0,\mu}
   \Bigr]
 \,+\,O(\varepsilon^{4}).
\label{eq:response}
\end{equation}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
Expand $S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a]$ in powers of $a_{\mu}$ using
(\ref{eq:Seff-def}); the linear term vanishes by gauge invariance
at the locked vacuum; the quadratic term, after plane-wave
substitution, collapses to the stated expression with
$\langle\cos^{2}(q\!\cdot\!x)\rangle=\tfrac{1}{2}$ absorbed into
the factor $\tfrac{1}{2}V$.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Extraction identities]
\label{cor:extract}
From three independent polarisation experiments
$(\hat{e}^{a}_{\mu},\hat{e}^{0}_{\mu})\in
 \{(\hat{e}^{(1)},0),\,(\hat{e}^{(2)},0),\,(0,\hat{e}^{(3)})\}$
at fixed $|q|\ll q_{0}$, the coefficients are extracted as
\begin{align}
c_{W}
 &\;=\;\frac{2}{V\,\varepsilon^{2}\,q^{2}}\,
       \Delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(1)}
       \;=\;\frac{2}{V\,\varepsilon^{2}\,q^{2}}\,
       \Delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(2)},\\
c_{B}
 &\;=\;\frac{2}{V\,\varepsilon^{2}\,q^{2}}\,
       \Delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(3)}.
\end{align}
The equality of the two $c_{W}$ estimates is a gauge-isotropy
consistency check.
\end{cor}

\subsection*{3. Consistency with Math44 Thm~cWcB}

\begin{thm}[Math46b--Math44 consistency]
\label{thm:consistency}
Under the Math40 locked triple and the Math43 matching scale
$\ell^{\star}=1$, the linear-response coefficients of
Def~\ref{defn:cWcB} satisfy
\begin{equation}
c_{W} \;=\; \frac{1}{96\pi^{2}},
\qquad
c_{B} \;=\; \frac{1}{64\pi^{2}},
\end{equation}
matching Math44 Thm~cWcB. The equality is a statement about
operators, not just numbers: the second functional derivative of
$\mathrm{Tr}\log$ at $a=0$ is the one-loop polarisation tensor that
Math44 \S 4 expands.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
Equations (\ref{eq:cW-def})--(\ref{eq:cB-def}) reproduce the
$O(a^{2})$ coefficient of the Math44 $\mathrm{Tr}\log$ expansion;
the Math44 Thm~cWcB computation is exactly the evaluation of that
$O(a^{2})$ term on the Brazovskii shell with $\ell=\ell^{\star}=1$.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{4. Falsification conditions}

\begin{prop}[Three failure modes]
\label{prop:fail}
A C3 extractor implementing Definition \ref{defn:cWcB} and
Corollary \ref{cor:extract} falsifies Math44 Thm~cWcB if any of the
following occurs on refined grids $N\in\{32,64,128\}$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(F1)] $c_{W}(N)$ does not converge to $1/(96\pi^{2})$ at rate
$\ge O(N^{-2})$.
\item[(F2)] $c_{B}(N)$ does not converge to $1/(64\pi^{2})$ at rate
$\ge O(N^{-2})$.
\item[(F3)] The two independent $c_{W}$ estimates
$(\hat{e}^{(1)},\hat{e}^{(2)})$ disagree by more than $1\%$
(gauge-isotropy breakdown).
\end{enumerate}
Any of (F1)--(F3) invalidates Math44.
\end{prop}

\subsection*{5. Interface specification for the C3 extractor}

A faithful Math46b-compliant C3 extractor must expose exactly the
following operations:

\begin{itemize}
\item[\textbf{E1.}] \texttt{load\_locked\_package(path)} ---
read the actual solver output: $(\Psi_{\mathrm{full}},
\rho_{\mathrm{BCC}},\ldots)$ from \texttt{.npy} files and
\texttt{metadata.json}.
\item[\textbf{E2.}] \texttt{project\_doublet(}$\Psi_{\mathrm{full}}$\texttt{)}
--- return $\Psi_{D}\in\mathbb{C}^{N^{3}\times 2}$ by the Math31
Class-III projection (which channels of the full field constitute
the doublet).
\item[\textbf{E3.}] \texttt{polar\_frame(}$\Psi_{D}$\texttt{)} ---
return $F_{0}(x)\in U(2)$ by polar decomposition with the
$U(1)_{\mathrm{em}}$ gauge \emph{exposed} (not silently fixed).
\item[\textbf{E4.}] \texttt{apply\_probe(}$F_{0}, a_{\mu}$\texttt{)} ---
return $F_{a}$ by the path-ordered exponential (\ref{eq:Fa-def}),
specialised to plane-wave probes.
\item[\textbf{E5.}] \texttt{compute\_Seff(}$F_{a},\psi$\texttt{)} ---
call the \emph{actual backend} Hessian $L_{\mathrm{full}}$
(family, locking, shell-bias, Class-II terms included) to compute
$\tfrac{1}{2}\mathrm{Tr}\log L_{\mathrm{full}}$ on the shell
$\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}$.
\item[\textbf{E6.}] \texttt{extract\_cWcB()} --- run three
polarisation experiments and apply Corollary \ref{cor:extract}.
\item[\textbf{E7.}] \texttt{audit\_T6()} --- return
$c_{W}\cdot 96\pi^{2}$, $c_{B}\cdot 64\pi^{2}$, the gauge-isotropy
ratio, and pass/fail flags per Proposition \ref{prop:fail}.
\end{itemize}

\begin{rmk}[What Math46 v0.1 did wrong, formally]
v0.1 implemented \emph{none} of E5 correctly (used a scalar
Brazovskii surrogate Hessian), skipped E4 entirely (no probe), and
collapsed E6 to a vacuum average of $\mathcal{F}^{(0) 2}$. All three
are structural, not cosmetic, failures.
\end{rmk}

\subsection*{6. Cost budget (probe-mode)}

Each plane-wave experiment requires one $\mathrm{Tr}\log
L_{\mathrm{full}}$ evaluation at $O(a^{0})$ and one at $O(a^{2})$.
On the shell $\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}$ the trace is approximated by
stochastic probes (Hutchinson) with $N_{s}\sim 32$ samples,
yielding $\approx 10^{-2}$ relative error. With three
polarisations and three grids $N\in\{32,64,128\}$, the total cost
is
\begin{equation}
C_{\mathrm{probe}}
 \;\approx\; 2\cdot N_{s}\cdot 3\cdot 3 \cdot C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N)
 \;\approx\; 180\cdot C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N),
\end{equation}
where $C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N)=O(N^{3}\log N)$ is one Hessian
application. At $N=128$ on a single A100 this is
$\sim 3$--$4$ hours wall-clock.

\subsection*{7. What remains (Math46b residual)}

(a) The Hutchinson trace-log estimator carries its own variance
floor; convergence to the $1\%$ audit threshold must be verified
empirically.

(b) Gauge-fixing of the probe polarisations (transversality
$\hat{e}^{a}_{\mu}q^{\mu}=0$) must be performed on-grid; non-zero
longitudinal components are absorbed by the gauge-isotropy check.

(c) The path-ordered exponential in (\ref{eq:Fa-def}) reduces to a
global multiplication for plane-wave probes; the generalisation to
curved-background probes (needed if Math47 introduces mixed
$h$-$\mathcal{F}$ operators) is deferred to a future addendum
(Math47 supplement).  The Math46c tag is reserved for the C2
extractor v2 redesign.

\subsection*{8. Records pointers}

\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}: theory tag
      \texttt{Math46b-probe-response-2026-04-16}.
\item \texttt{docs/math/TECT-Math46.tex.txt}: cross-reference
      added in \S 3 --- the advertised $c_{W},c_{B}$ extraction is
      \emph{only} valid through the probe-mode driver defined
      here.
\item The withdrawn \texttt{math46\_c3\_extractor.py} header is
      updated to cite Math46b as a hard prerequisite.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{9. Addendum: v0.3--v0.5 extractor amendments
(tags Math46b-c3-extractor-v0.3 \ldots v0.5)}

The \texttt{math46\_c3\_extractor.py} implementation passed through
three peer-review rounds after the withdrawn v0.1.  The definitive
formal content of the v0.3--v0.5 amendments is recorded here so that
the theory note tracks the production code in a single place.

\paragraph{v0.3 reformulation (D1--D4).}

Version v0.3 replaced the v0.2 path-ordered Wilson-line probe
(whose straight-line primitive $I(x)=(\hat{e}\!\cdot\!x)\,
\mathrm{sinc}(q\!\cdot\!x)$ is not globally periodic on
$\mathbb{T}^{3}$ for transverse $\epsilon$) by a Fourier-space
covariant-derivative perturbation of the full Hessian
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:cov-pert-def}
  L(\epsilon) \;=\; L_{\mathrm{full}}
  \;+\; \epsilon\, M_{1}[a]
  \;+\; \epsilon^{2}\, M_{2}[a],
  \qquad
  a_{\mu}(x) \;=\; \epsilon_{\mu}\cos(q\!\cdot\!x),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
  M_{1}[a]\,v \;=\; 2\mathrm{i}\,a_{\mu}T\,(\partial_{\mu}v)
  + \mathrm{i}\,(\partial_{\mu}a_{\mu})\,T\,v,
  \qquad
  M_{2}[a]\,v \;=\; (a_{\mu}a^{\mu})\,T^{2}\,v,
\end{equation}
and $T = T^{a}$ the doublet generator on the metadata-locked
two-channel subspace.  The objects are strictly periodic, so the
torus boundary artefacts which forced the withdrawal of v0.2 are
absent by construction.  Item-level specification:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.7em]
\item[\textbf{D1.}] The identification of the doublet subspace
      $\mathcal{H}_{D}\subset\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{full}}$ is
      \emph{fail-closed}: \texttt{metadata['doublet\_channels']} is
      mandatory; the extractor rejects any package without it.
\item[\textbf{D2.}] Former \texttt{polar\_frame} is renamed
      \texttt{frame\_lift}; it returns the Householder-completed
      $U(2)$ frame together with the integer phase winding of
      $\det F_{0}$ along each lattice axis (topological charge of
      the locked vacuum).
\item[\textbf{D3.}] \texttt{apply\_probe} is replaced by
      (\ref{eq:cov-pert-def}) above; the v0.2 Wilson-line primitive
      is discarded.
\item[\textbf{D4.}] The Lanczos Tr$\log$ kernel reports
      \texttt{negative\_ritz\_count} without silent flooring, and
      $\Delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{sym}}
      =\tfrac{1}{2}[\Delta S(+\epsilon)+\Delta S(-\epsilon)]$
      is the reported observable.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{v0.4 interface closure (P1--P3).}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.7em]
\item[\textbf{P1.}] \texttt{ActualBackendAdapter} exposes
      $\pi\circ H_{\mathrm{full}}\circ\iota$ where
      $\iota:\mathcal{H}_{D}\hookrightarrow\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{full}}$
      is the metadata-channel embedding and $\pi=\iota^{\dagger}$
      its adjoint.
\item[\textbf{P2.}] \texttt{perturbed\_hessian\_vec\_factory} is
      fail-closed on the covariant coupling $M_{1},M_{2}$: silent
      fall-through to a kinetic-Laplacian surrogate is eliminated;
      \texttt{allow\_surrogate=True} is a debug-only escape hatch
      that is recorded in the JSON \texttt{compliance} block.
\item[\textbf{P3.}] Production CLI + \texttt{load\_backend()}
      restored; the synthetic harness is demoted to an internal
      \texttt{\_smoke\_test()}.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{v0.5 accuracy fixes (Q1--Q3).}
These three items are \emph{theorem-level} corrections, not merely
engineering patches; each is stated as a proposition below.

\begin{prop}[Shell-restricted Han--Avron--Saad prefactor, Q1]
\label{prop:han-avron-saad}
Let $A$ be a Hermitian operator on $\mathbb{C}^{n}$ and
$P_{\Sigma}=P_{\Sigma}^{2}=P_{\Sigma}^{\dagger}$ the orthogonal
projector onto the Brazovskii shell
$\Sigma_{q_{0},\Delta}\subset\widehat{\mathbb{T}}^{3}$.  Let
$v_{0}=P_{\Sigma} z$ where $z$ is a complex Rademacher vector on
$\mathbb{C}^{n}$ (so that $\mathbb{E}[zz^{\dagger}]=I_{n}$), and let
$T_{m}\in\mathbb{R}^{m\times m}$ be the tridiagonal Lanczos
matrix generated from the unit vector $q_{1}=v_{0}/\lVert
v_{0}\rVert$ with $m$ steps applied to $A$.  Then the $m$-step
Han--Avron--Saad log estimator
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{L}_{m}(v_{0})
  \;:=\;
  \lVert v_{0}\rVert^{2}\,\sum_{k=1}^{m}U_{1k}^{2}\,\log\theta_{k},
  \qquad T_{m}=U\,\mathrm{diag}(\theta_{k})\,U^{T},
\end{equation}
satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb{E}\!\bigl[\widehat{L}_{m}(v_{0})\bigr]
  \;\xrightarrow[m\to\infty]{}\;
  \mathrm{Tr}\bigl(P_{\Sigma}\log(A)\,P_{\Sigma}\bigr)
  \;=\;
  \mathrm{Tr}\log\bigl(A\bigr|_{\Sigma}\bigr).
\end{equation}
In particular the correct prefactor is
$\lVert v_{0}\rVert^{2}=\langle v_{0},v_{0}\rangle$, \emph{not} the
ambient dimension $n$.  The latter coincides with
$\lVert v_{0}\rVert^{2}$ only in the unrestricted case
$P_{\Sigma}=I$; on the shell it over-counts by the fill-fraction
factor $n/\lVert v_{0}\rVert^{2}\approx f_{\Sigma}^{-1}$, where
$f_{\Sigma}=\lvert\Sigma\rvert/n$ is the shell occupation.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
$\mathbb{E}[v_{0}v_{0}^{\dagger}]=P_{\Sigma}$; therefore
$\mathbb{E}[\langle v_{0},f(A)v_{0}\rangle]
=\mathrm{Tr}(P_{\Sigma}f(A)P_{\Sigma})$ for any analytic $f$.  The
Lanczos identity
$\langle v_{0},f(A)v_{0}\rangle
=\lVert v_{0}\rVert^{2}e_{1}^{T}f(T_{m})e_{1}+O(m^{-c})$
for the Hermitian $A$ (Saad, \emph{Numerical Methods for Large
Eigenvalue Problems}, Ch.~13) then gives the estimator as stated.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[Symmetrised $\Delta S$ error propagation, Q2]
\label{prop:dS-variance}
Let $\widehat{S}_{+},\widehat{S}_{0},\widehat{S}_{-}$ be
independent unbiased estimators of
$S(\pm\epsilon), S(0)$ with variances
$\sigma_{+}^{2},\sigma_{0}^{2},\sigma_{-}^{2}$.  Define
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\Delta S}_{\mathrm{sym}}
  \;:=\;
  \tfrac{1}{2}\bigl[(\widehat{S}_{+}-\widehat{S}_{0})
  +(\widehat{S}_{-}-\widehat{S}_{0})\bigr]
  \;=\;
  \tfrac{1}{2}\widehat{S}_{+}
  +\tfrac{1}{2}\widehat{S}_{-}
  -\widehat{S}_{0}.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
  \mathrm{Var}\bigl(\widehat{\Delta S}_{\mathrm{sym}}\bigr)
  \;=\;
  \tfrac{1}{4}\sigma_{+}^{2}
  +\tfrac{1}{4}\sigma_{-}^{2}
  +\sigma_{0}^{2}
  \;=\;
  \tfrac{1}{4}\bigl(\sigma_{+}^{2}+\sigma_{-}^{2}+4\sigma_{0}^{2}\bigr).
\end{equation}
The v0.4 implementation used the coefficient $2$ in place of $4$
on $\sigma_{0}^{2}$, under-weighting the zero-field noise.
\end{prop}

\begin{prop}[Doublet/full-shape adapter identity, Q3]
\label{prop:shape-adapter}
Let $\iota:\mathcal{H}_{D}\hookrightarrow\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{full}}$
be the metadata-channel embedding and $\pi=\iota^{\dagger}$ its
adjoint.  For a covariant coupling $M_{\ell}[a]$ acting on
$\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{full}}$ via the doublet generator
$T\in\mathrm{End}(\mathcal{H}_{D})$ extended by zero on
$\mathcal{H}_{D}^{\perp}$,
\begin{equation}
  \pi\circ M_{\ell}[a]\circ\iota
  \;=\;
  M_{\ell}^{D}[a],
  \qquad
  \ell\in\{1,2\},
\end{equation}
where $M_{\ell}^{D}[a]$ is the same operator regarded on
$\mathcal{H}_{D}$ directly.  Consequently, if a production backend
returns $M_{\ell}[a]v_{D}$ in full shape $(C,N,N,N)$, restricting
via $\pi$ produces the same doublet-shape vector that the
extractor's probe-space matvec expects; no physics is lost.  The
v0.5 native-backend branch therefore accepts both return shapes
and reduces to $M_{\ell}^{D}[a]v_{D}$ in either case.
\end{prop}

The three corrections are mutually independent but all three must
hold simultaneously for the extracted $c_{W},c_{B},Z_{h}$ to equal
their Math44 / Math45 targets to $O(10^{-2})$; Proposition
\ref{prop:han-avron-saad} alone accounts for a systematic bias of
order $f_{\Sigma}^{-1}$ (typically $\sim 10^{2}$ on a standard
$N=64$ shell) in the unshifted v0.4 Tr$\log$ output.

\paragraph{v0.6 completeness closure (R1--R3).}

These three items are audit-completeness and payload-semantics
corrections on top of the v0.5 numerical core; the Q1--Q3
propositions above are retained unchanged.

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.7em]
\item[\textbf{R1.}] Compliance semantics.  The JSON field
      \texttt{compliance.fail\_closed\_E4} is defined by
      \begin{equation*}
        \texttt{fail\_closed\_E4}
        \;\Leftrightarrow\;
        \neg\,\texttt{uses\_surrogate\_M1M2},
      \end{equation*}
      where \texttt{uses\_surrogate\_M1M2} is the disjunction of the
      per-probe surrogate flags returned by
      \texttt{perturbed\_hessian\_vec\_factory}.  v0.5 hard-coded
      this field to $\top$, which misreported
      \texttt{allow\_surrogate=True} runs.
\item[\textbf{R2.}] CLI metadata tracks the module version:
      \texttt{argparse} description ``v0.6 production'' and
      \texttt{--out} default \texttt{math46\_c3\_audit\_v0\_6.json}.
\item[\textbf{R3.}] Frame-singularity audit.  The Householder lift
      $F_{0}(x)$ is stabilised at $\lVert\psi_{D}(x)\rVert <
      \varepsilon_{\mathrm{floor}}=10^{-14}$ by a division by
      $\max(\lVert\psi_{D}\rVert,\varepsilon_{\mathrm{floor}})$.
      Points $x$ where $\lVert\psi_{D}(x)\rVert$ is vanishingly
      small constitute doublet \emph{nodes} at which the frame
      direction is geometrically ill-defined and the lift is
      silently fictitious.  v0.6 promotes this to an explicit audit
      predicate,
      \begin{equation}
        \texttt{pass\_frame\_nonzero}
        \;\Leftrightarrow\;
        \min_{x\in\mathbb{T}^{3}_{N}}
          \bigl\lVert\psi_{D}(x)\bigr\rVert
        \;>\; 10^{-10},
      \end{equation}
      and emits both \texttt{min\_norm} and the predicate in the CLI
      \texttt{frame\_audit} block.  A failed predicate does not
      automatically void the extracted $c_{W},c_{B}$ but must be
      flagged downstream as a Class-II geometric risk.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{v0.7 final-closure (R4--R5).}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.7em]
\item[\textbf{R4.}] \emph{$\mathtt{pass\_T6\_final}$ gate.}
      The spectral-numeric audit predicate $\mathtt{pass\_T6}$ is
      necessary but not sufficient for a valid extraction: a doublet
      node (site $x_{0}$ with $\lVert\psi_{D}(x_{0})\rVert < 10^{-10}$)
      silently corrupts the Householder frame lift and therefore the
      extracted $c_{W},c_{B}$ even when $\mathtt{pass\_T6}=\top$.  The
      production-go/no-go predicate is therefore
      \begin{equation}
        \mathtt{pass\_T6\_final}
        \;\Leftrightarrow\;
        \mathtt{pass\_T6}
        \;\wedge\;
        \mathtt{pass\_frame\_nonzero},
      \end{equation}
      which is injected (together with $\mathtt{pass\_frame\_nonzero}$)
      into the CLI \texttt{audit} JSON block.
\item[\textbf{R5.}] \emph{$\mathtt{\_SmokeBackend}$ full-field contract.}
      The smoke backend \texttt{hessian\_vec} previously read
      $N=v.\mathtt{shape}[0]$ and applied FFT on axes $(0,1,2)$,
      consistent with a doublet-shape $(N,N,N,2)$ input.  The actual
      adapter calls \texttt{hessian\_vec\_full} with full-field tensors
      of shape $(C,N,N,N)$; v0.7 unpacks $(\mathtt{\_C},N,\_,\_)$ and
      applies FFT on axes $(1,2,3)$ with $K^{2}$ broadcast as $(1,N,N,N)$.
      The smoke test now exercises the identical code path as production.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Updated records pointer (v0.3--v0.7).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}: theory tags
      \texttt{Math46b-c3-extractor-v0.3-2026-04-16},
      \texttt{...-v0.4-2026-04-16},
      \texttt{...-v0.5-2026-04-16},
      \texttt{...-v0.6-2026-04-16},
      \texttt{...-v0.7-2026-04-16}.
\item \texttt{PDE/stamp\_version\_headers.py}:
      \texttt{math46\_c3\_extractor.py = v0.7}.
\item \texttt{Website/data/version\_index.json}:
      current tag
      \texttt{Math46b-c3-extractor-v0.7-2026-04-16}.
\end{itemize}

\end{document}

%    (ii) probed K_{ij}(p) with a rank-1 delta-function source
%         that does not populate the symmetric tensor sector;
%    (iii) lifted to strain space with the wrong index structure
%         (H_eps = -p_k p_l K_ij rather than a projection onto
%         a genuine tensor probe basis);

%         hardcoded placeholder.
%

%    output package and the actual backend Hessian, (b)
%    constructing six independent symmetric-tensor probe
%    tangents from geometric deformations of the locked
%    background, (c) projecting L_full onto that basis to
%    obtain a 6x6 block Hessian whose TT sector defines the
%    graviton kinetic term, and (d) defining T1/T2/T3 as
%    operational functionals of that projected block.

%         Math46 §2 (C2 extractor design);

\begin{document}

\section*{Math46c: Probe-tangent / projected-Hessian redesign
of the Math46 C2 (gravity) extractor}

\subsection*{0. Motivation and principles}

The Math46 v0.1 C2 extractor failed an internal audit on five
structural grounds (enumerated in the withdrawn file header).
The underlying pathology was conceptual: a gravitational kinetic
coefficient is a response function of the \emph{actual} effective
action to \emph{symmetric tensor} deformations of the locked
background, not a vacuum moment of any scalar proxy. Math46c
re-founds the extractor on four non-negotiable principles.

\begin{description}
\item[(P1) Load the actual solver package.]
No surrogate fields, no reconstructed locked state; only the
frozen artefacts of the Q-class solver run (the locked field
$\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}$ as \texttt{.npy}, \texttt{config.json},
\texttt{metadata.json}, and any saved shell data $\hat{n},
\{G\}$).
\item[(P2) Load the actual backend and call its Hessian.]
The projected Hessian is assembled by repeated calls to
\texttt{hessian\_vec}$(\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}},v)$ of the genuine
solver backend (family + locking + shell-bias + Class-II terms).
No Brazovskii scalar surrogate is admissible.
\item[(P3) Probe tangents are geometric and direct.]
Each symmetric-tensor probe $E^{(\alpha)}$ acts on the locked
background as an infinitesimal affine deformation
$x\mapsto(I+\varepsilon E^{(\alpha)})x$, realised on-grid by FFT
resampling of $\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}$. No delta-function or
plane-wave pointwise $\Psi$-space perturbation is admissible.
\item[(P4) The observable is a projected low-energy Hessian.]
The T1/T2/T3 audits are functionals of the $6\times 6$ matrix
obtained by sandwiching $L_{\mathrm{full}}$ between the six
symmetric-tensor probe tangents, block-decomposed per the
irreducible representations of $SO(3)_{\hat p}$.
\end{description}

Principles (P1)--(P4) are the operational form of the Math45
Einstein closure: on the locked vacuum the emergent metric
fluctuation is a \emph{soft-mode} of a symmetric tensor
deformation of the order-parameter condensate, and its
kinetic coefficient is read off the response of $L_{\mathrm{full}}$
to geometric probes, not of any scalar proxy.

\subsection*{1. Package and backend adapters}

\begin{defn}[Solver package]
\label{defn:solver-package}
A \emph{solver package} is a directory containing at minimum
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}\in\mathbb{C}^{N^{3}\times c_{\mathrm{full}}}
 \quad(\text{\texttt{.npy}}),\quad
\texttt{config.json},\quad \texttt{metadata.json},
\]
and optionally the frozen Brazovskii shell data
$\hat n\in S^{2}$ and reciprocal vectors
$\{G_{j}\}_{j=1}^{n_{G}}\subset\mathbb{R}^{3}$.
The lattice spacing $dx$, side $N$, and channel count
$c_{\mathrm{full}}$ are recovered from \texttt{config.json}.
No attribute of the package may be recomputed inside the
extractor; the package is immutable input.
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[Actual backend adapter]
\label{defn:backend}
An \emph{actual backend adapter} is an object exposing exactly
two operations on the package's locked field:
\begin{align}
\texttt{residual}(\Psi)&\;\in\;\mathbb{R}^{+}, &
   \texttt{residual}(\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}})&<10^{-6},\\
\texttt{hessian\_vec}(\Psi,v)&\;=\;L_{\mathrm{full}}[\Psi]\,v,
\end{align}
where $L_{\mathrm{full}}[\Psi]=\delta^{2}S/\delta\bar\Psi\,\delta\Psi$
is the genuine second variation of the solver's Euclidean action
(family, locking term, shell-bias, and any Class-II corrections
included). No substitute is admissible.
\end{defn}

\subsection*{2. Geometric probe tangents}

Fix a non-zero probe momentum $p\in\mathbb{R}^{3}$ with
$|p|\ll q_{0}$ (soft-mode window) and a unit vector
$\hat p=p/|p|$. Complete $\hat p$ to an orthonormal triad
$(\hat p,\hat e_{1},\hat e_{2})$.

\begin{defn}[Six-fold symmetric-tensor probe basis]
\label{defn:probe-basis}
Define six symmetric traceless-or-trace tensors
$E^{(\alpha)}\in\mathrm{Sym}_{2}(\mathbb{R}^{3})$,
$\alpha\in\{TT1,TT2,V1,V2,\mathrm{tr},L\}$, adapted to $\hat p$:
\begin{align}
E^{(TT1)} &= \hat e_{1}\!\otimes\!\hat e_{2}
             + \hat e_{2}\!\otimes\!\hat e_{1},\\
E^{(TT2)} &= \hat e_{1}\!\otimes\!\hat e_{1}
             - \hat e_{2}\!\otimes\!\hat e_{2},\\
E^{(V1)}  &= \hat p\!\otimes\!\hat e_{1}
             + \hat e_{1}\!\otimes\!\hat p,\\
E^{(V2)}  &= \hat p\!\otimes\!\hat e_{2}
             + \hat e_{2}\!\otimes\!\hat p,\\
E^{(\mathrm{tr})} &= \tfrac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\,I_{3},\\
E^{(L)}   &= \hat p\!\otimes\!\hat p
             -\tfrac{1}{3}I_{3}.
\end{align}
The pair $\{E^{(TT1)},E^{(TT2)}\}$ spans the transverse-traceless
(spin-2) sector, $\{E^{(V1)},E^{(V2)}\}$ the vector (spin-1)
sector, and $\{E^{(\mathrm{tr})},E^{(L)}\}$ the scalar (spin-0)
sector of the $SO(3)_{\hat p}$ decomposition.
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[Affine-deformation tangent]
\label{defn:tangent}
Given $E\in\mathrm{Sym}_{2}(\mathbb{R}^{3})$ and
$p\in\mathbb{R}^{3}$, the probe tangent is the on-grid FFT
realisation of
\begin{equation}
v_{E,p}(x) \;:=\; \lim_{\varepsilon\to 0}
  \frac{1}{\varepsilon}\bigl[
    \Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}\!\bigl((I+\varepsilon\,E\cos(p\!\cdot\!x))\,x\bigr)
    -\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}(x)
  \bigr],
\label{eq:tangent-def}
\end{equation}
computed spectrally as
\begin{equation}
v_{E,p}(x)
 = \mathcal{F}^{-1}\!\Bigl[\,
     i\bigl(E\cdot k\bigr)_{i}\,k_{j}\,
     \text{(phase shift)}\cdots
   \Bigr](x),
\end{equation}
with the operator implemented by finite-difference
$(\varepsilon=10^{-5})$ of the map
$\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}\mapsto\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}\circ
(I+\varepsilon E)$ on the discrete torus. Translation invariance
of the locked state implies $v_{E,p}$ has exactly Fourier
support $\pm p$.
\end{defn}

\begin{rmk}
The translation tangents $t_{i}(x):=\partial_{i}\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}(x)$
span a three-dimensional null subspace of $L_{\mathrm{full}}$ (the
Goldstones of broken translations); the projector
$P_{\perp}=I-\sum_{i}|t_{i}\rangle\langle t_{i}|/\langle t_{i}|t_{i}\rangle$
with \texttt{projector\_tol}$=10^{-10}$ must be applied to every
probe tangent before Hessian evaluation.
\end{rmk}

\subsection*{3. Projected Hessian and block decomposition}

\begin{defn}[Projected low-energy Hessian]
\label{defn:H-block}
For a fixed $p$ with orthonormal triad, assemble
$v_{\alpha}:=P_{\perp}\,v_{E^{(\alpha)},p}$ and compute
\begin{equation}
H_{\alpha\beta}(p)
 \;:=\;\Re\bigl\langle v_{\alpha},\,
   L_{\mathrm{full}}\,v_{\beta}\bigr\rangle,
\qquad
G_{\alpha\beta}(p)
 \;:=\;\Re\bigl\langle v_{\alpha},\,v_{\beta}\bigr\rangle.
\label{eq:HG-def}
\end{equation}
The physical spectrum is the generalised eigenproblem
\begin{equation}
H(p)\,u \;=\; \lambda(p)\,G(p)\,u,
\qquad u\in\mathbb{R}^{6}.
\label{eq:genev}
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

The $SO(3)_{\hat p}$-block structure of $H(p)$ is
\begin{equation}
H(p)
 \;=\;
 \begin{pmatrix}
  H_{TT}(p) & 0 & 0\\
  0 & H_{V}(p) & H_{V\mathrm{tr}}(p)\\
  0 & H_{V\mathrm{tr}}(p)^{\!\top} & H_{S}(p)
 \end{pmatrix}
 \;+\;\Delta H(p),
\label{eq:blockform}
\end{equation}
where $H_{TT}\in\mathbb{R}^{2\times 2}$, $H_{V}\in\mathbb{R}^{2\times 2}$,
$H_{S}\in\mathbb{R}^{2\times 2}$, and $\Delta H(p)$ is the
inter-sector mixing matrix whose norm quantifies residual
gauge / lattice artefacts.

\subsection*{4. Operational definitions of T1, T2, T3}

\begin{defn}[T1: purity / block-diagonality]
\label{defn:T1}
The \emph{purity} audit is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{T}_{1}(p)
 \;:=\;\frac{\lVert\Delta H(p)\rVert_{F}}
            {\lVert H(p)\rVert_{F}}
 \;\stackrel{!}{\le}\;10^{-2}.
\end{equation}
Failure of T1 signals either incomplete projection off the
translation Goldstones or rotational anisotropy of the BCC
lattice intruding into the soft-mode window.
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[T2: Einstein-type normalisation]
\label{defn:T2}
Let $\lambda_{TT,\min}(p)$ denote the smaller generalised
eigenvalue of the $2\times 2$ block $(H_{TT}(p),G_{TT}(p))$.
The \emph{graviton kinetic coefficient} is extracted by
small-$p$ fit:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{TT,\min}(p) \;=\; Z_{h}\,p^{2}\,+\,O(p^{4}),
\qquad
\frac{1}{16\pi G_{N}}\;=\;Z_{h}.
\label{eq:ZHfit}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, via Math45, $\kappa_{G}^{-2}=2Z_{h}=|Z|$ on
the locked triple.
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[T3: universality of the graviton coupling]
\label{defn:T3}
Given a set of transverse-traceless polarisations
$\{E^{(TT,i)}\}_{i=1}^{n_{p}}$ (any two linearly independent
TT tensors at each $p$, plus rotations of $p$ on the BCC
orbit), extract $Z_{h}^{(\alpha,\beta)}$ from each
polarisation pair $(\alpha,\beta)$. The \emph{universality
defect} is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{univ}}
 \;:=\;\sup_{\alpha,\beta}\bigl|
   Z_{h}^{(\alpha,\beta)}-\bar Z_{h}
 \bigr|/\bar Z_{h}
 \;\stackrel{!}{\le}\;10^{-2},
\end{equation}
with $\bar Z_{h}$ the mean. Failure of T3 refutes the
universal character of the emergent Einstein coupling asserted
by Math45 Thm~kappaG.
\end{defn}

\subsection*{5. Consistency with Math45}

\begin{thm}[Math46c--Math45 consistency]
\label{thm:M46c-M45}
Under the Math40 locked triple $(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=
(0.26,-0.43,+1.62)$ with $(Z,Y)=(-1,+\tfrac{1}{2})$ and
$Yq_{0}^{2}/|Z|=\tfrac{1}{2}$, the coefficient $Z_{h}$ extracted
via Definition~\ref{defn:T2} in the continuum limit
$N\to\infty,\;p\to 0$ satisfies
\begin{equation}
Z_{h} \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,\kappa_{G}^{-2} \;=\; \tfrac{|Z|}{2}
       \;=\; Yq_{0}^{2},
\end{equation}
matching Math45 Thm~kappaG. Conversely, any deviation
$|Z_{h}-|Z|/2|/|Z|>10^{-2}$ after joint $N$--$p$ extrapolation
falsifies the Einstein-closure claim of Math45.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
The probe tangent (\ref{eq:tangent-def}) is, by construction,
the linear response of $\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}$ under the
diffeomorphism $x\mapsto(I+\varepsilon E\cos p\!\cdot\!x)x$.
Substituting into $S[\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}+\varepsilon v_{E,p}]$
and expanding to $O(\varepsilon^{2})$, the coefficient of the
TT mode reproduces the Math45 \S 3 polarisation tensor at
external momentum $p$, whose small-$p$ limit is $Z_{h}p^{2}$
with $Z_{h}=Yq_{0}^{2}$.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{6. Falsification conditions}

\begin{prop}[C2 v2 failure modes]
\label{prop:C2fail}
A Math46c-compliant extractor falsifies Math45 Thm~kappaG on
refined grids $N\in\{32,64,128\}$ if any of the following
occurs:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(G1)] $\mathcal{T}_{1}(p)>10^{-2}$ in the soft-mode
      window $|p|\in[2\pi/(N dx),\,0.1\,q_{0}]$.
\item[(G2)] $Z_{h}(N)$ does not converge to $|Z|/2$ at rate
      $\ge O(N^{-2})$.
\item[(G3)] $\Delta_{\mathrm{univ}}>10^{-2}$ after
      polarisation / rotation averaging.
\end{enumerate}
Any of (G1)--(G3) invalidates Math45.
\end{prop}

\subsection*{7. Implementation discipline}

A Math46c-compliant rewrite of \texttt{math46\_c2\_extractor.py}
must follow exactly the following discipline; each operation
cites the theorem or definition that justifies it.

\begin{description}
\item[Step 1 (package).] Load the solver package
per Def~\ref{defn:solver-package}; verify
$\texttt{residual}(\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}})<10^{-6}$ using the
backend of Def~\ref{defn:backend}. No re-solve.
\item[Step 2 (Goldstone projector).] Build translation tangents
$t_{i}=\partial_{i}\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}$ by spectral derivative;
construct $P_{\perp}$ to tolerance $10^{-10}$.
\item[Step 3 (probe tangents).] For each audited $p$, construct
the six $v_{\alpha}$ of Def~\ref{defn:tangent} via FFT-resampled
finite difference with $\varepsilon_{\mathrm{fd}}=10^{-5}$; apply
$P_{\perp}$.
\item[Step 4 (projected Hessian).] Assemble $H(p),G(p)$ by 36
calls to \texttt{hessian\_vec} and 36 inner products per $p$
per Def~\ref{defn:H-block}.
\item[Step 5 (audit).] Evaluate T1, T2, T3 per
Defs~\ref{defn:T1}--\ref{defn:T3}; compare to
Prop~\ref{prop:C2fail} thresholds; emit pass/fail with
numerical residuals.
\end{description}

No step may be shortcut by a scalar / Brazovskii surrogate; no
probe may be injected directly in $\Psi$-space as a
$\delta$-function or rank-1 tensor; no strain-space lift of
the form $H_{\varepsilon}\sim-p_{k}p_{l}K_{ij}$ is admissible.
These were the exact failure modes of the withdrawn v0.1.

\subsection*{8. Cost budget (C2 v2)}

Per probe momentum $p$: 6 FFT-resampled tangent constructions
$+$ 36 backend \texttt{hessian\_vec} calls $+$ 36 inner
products $+$ one $6\times 6$ generalised eigensolve. At
$N=128$ on a single A100 and a backend Hessian cost
$C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(128)\sim 0.5$--$1$~s per call, one momentum
requires $\sim 20$--$40$~s; a 12-momentum audit
($3$ magnitudes $\times$ $4$ BCC-symmetric directions) runs
in $\sim 5$--$10$~min per grid, i.e.\ $\sim 15$--$30$~min total
across $\{32,64,128\}$. Memory: dominated by six copies of
$\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}$ per $p$, $6\cdot c_{\mathrm{full}}\cdot
N^{3}\cdot 16$ bytes $\approx 6$ GB at $N=128,c_{\mathrm{full}}=4$.

\subsection*{9. What remains (Math46c residual)}

(a) The Python skeleton implementing Steps~1--5 is pending
user delivery; no scaffolded code is deposited.

(b) The BCC rotational orbit of $p$ needed for T3 averaging
must be chosen to respect the lattice point group $O_{h}$ (not
the full $SO(3)$); polarisation pairs within an orbit are
equivalent by lattice symmetry.

(c) The C3 extractor rewrite (Math46b E1--E7) proceeds in
parallel and independently; joint consistency of T2 ($Z_{h}$)
with T6 ($c_{W},c_{B}$) at the same $(N,p,\ell^{\star})$ is
deferred to a Math47 combined-closure note.

\subsection*{10. Records pointers}

\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}: theory tag
      \texttt{Math46c-c2-probe-tangent-2026-04-16}.
\item \texttt{PDE/math46\_c2\_extractor.py}: withdrawn header
      updated to cite Math46c as a hard prerequisite.
\item \texttt{docs/math/TECT-Math46b.tex.txt} \S 7(c): Math46c
      tag reservation for the C2 v2 redesign --- now consumed.
\item \texttt{docs/status/research-log.md}: Math46c entry.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{11. Addendum: v0.3--v0.7 extractor amendments
(tags Math46c-c2-extractor-v0.3 \ldots v0.7)}

This addendum records the theorem-level content of the
\texttt{math46\_c2\_extractor.py} revisions v0.3 through v0.7, in
one-to-one correspondence with the production code.

\paragraph{v0.5 amendments (P-A, P-B).}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.7em]
\item[\textbf{P-A.}] Introduction of the cross-sector H mixing
      diagnostic (H0 falsification mode) as a new argument of
      \textbf{Prop.C2fail}; distinct from the Gram mixing
      $\mu_{ss'}$ (G1 diagnostic).
\item[\textbf{P-B.}] Runtime audit-level consistency between the
      Fourier-periodic tangent (default) and the spectral tangent
      as companion probe (Pb diagnostic):
      $\delta Z_{\text{probe}}
      = |Z_{h}^{\mathrm{fourier}}-Z_{h}^{\mathrm{spectral}}|
      /|Z_{h}^{\mathrm{fourier}}|$.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{v0.6 hot-fixes (F1, F2, F3).}
Purely operational fixes (NameError on empty TT branch, docstring
alignment, and $\texttt{probe\_consistency\_mode}=\texttt{probe\_mode}$
fail-safe); no theorem-level change.

\paragraph{v0.7 basis-invariance closure (A, B, C).}

\begin{prop}[Basis-invariant H0 diagnostic, v0.7 Patch A]
\label{prop:C2fail-H0}
Let $G, H\in\mathbb{C}^{d\times d}$ be Hermitian with $G\succ 0$,
and let $\{P_{s}\}_{s\in\mathcal{S}}$ be the probe-basis projectors
onto the $O_{h}$ irrep sectors
$\mathcal{S}=\{\mathrm{TT},\mathrm{V},\mathrm{tr},\mathrm{L}\}$,
with block decompositions
$G_{ss}=P_{s}GP_{s}$, $H_{ss'}=P_{s}HP_{s'}$.  Define the
Gram-whitened cross-sector blocks
\begin{equation}
  \widetilde H_{ss'}
  \;:=\; G_{ss}^{-1/2}\,H_{ss'}\,G_{s's'}^{-1/2}
  \;\in\; \mathbb{C}^{d_{s}\times d_{s'}},
\end{equation}
and the Frobenius diagnostic
\begin{equation}
  \widetilde\nu_{ss'}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{\lVert\widetilde H_{ss'}\rVert_{F}}
       {\sqrt{\,\lVert\widetilde H_{ss}\rVert_{F}\,
              \lVert\widetilde H_{s's'}\rVert_{F}\,}}.
\end{equation}
Then $\widetilde\nu_{ss'}$ is invariant under \emph{independent}
rescalings $P_{s}\mapsto c_{s}P_{s}$ ($c_{s}\in\mathbb{R}_{>0}$) of
the probe basis in each sector, which leave the generalised
eigenproblem $H_{ss}v=\lambda G_{ss}v$ invariant (up to a trivial
rescaling of $v$).  The raw ratio
$\nu_{ss'}=\lVert H_{ss'}\rVert_F /
\sqrt{\lVert H_{ss}\rVert_F \lVert H_{s's'}\rVert_F}$
used in v0.5/v0.6 is invariant only under the global rescaling
$c_{s}\equiv c$.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
Under $P_{s}\mapsto c_{s}P_{s}$ one has
$G_{ss}\mapsto c_{s}^{2}G_{ss}$,
$H_{ss'}\mapsto c_{s}c_{s'}H_{ss'}$, hence
$G_{ss}^{-1/2}\mapsto c_{s}^{-1}G_{ss}^{-1/2}$ and
\begin{equation*}
  \widetilde H_{ss'}
  \;\mapsto\;
  (c_{s}^{-1}G_{ss}^{-1/2})\,(c_{s}c_{s'}H_{ss'})\,(c_{s'}^{-1}G_{s's'}^{-1/2})
  \;=\;
  \widetilde H_{ss'}.
\end{equation*}
Each Frobenius norm is therefore invariant, and so is
$\widetilde\nu_{ss'}$.  The raw ratio carries a factor
$\lvert c_{s}c_{s'}\rvert/\sqrt{c_{s}^{2}c_{s'}^{2}}=1$ only when
$c_{s}=c_{s'}$.
\end{proof}

\textbf{Consequence.}  In the v0.7 extractor the H0 falsification
mode of \textbf{Prop.C2fail} must be read with
$\widetilde\nu_{ss'}\le\mathtt{audit\_tol}$, not $\nu_{ss'}$.  The
Gram-whitened blocks are exactly the ones diagonalised by the
generalised eigensolver \texttt{sector\_generalised\_eigs}, so
\textbf{code-theory parity} is now achieved: the mixing diagnostic
and the reported spectrum are computed on the same linear-algebra
object $G_{ss}^{-1/2}H\,G_{s's'}^{-1/2}$.

\paragraph{v0.7 Patches B, C (operational).}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.7em]
\item[\textbf{B.}] \texttt{load\_backend()} is fail-closed on the
      Math46c E5 contract symbol \texttt{hessian\_vec}: the importer
      raises \texttt{AttributeError} immediately if the symbol is
      missing, rather than surfacing an opaque matvec failure later.
\item[\textbf{C.}] The CLI default output filename tracks the
      module version: \texttt{math46\_c2\_audit\_v0\_7.json}.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{v0.8 polish (S).}
The $Z_{h}$ aggregate over probe momenta was declared as a
$p^{2}$-weighted mean in the code comment but implemented as an
unweighted mean \texttt{np.mean}.  v0.8 implements the stated
estimator
\begin{equation}
  Z_{h}^{\mathrm{fit}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{\sum_{p^{2}>0} p^{2}\,Z_{h}(p)}
       {\sum_{p^{2}>0} p^{2}},
\end{equation}
excluding zero-momentum modes from the admissible set.  The
$p^{2}$ weighting is motivated by the continuum relation
$Z_{h}(p)\approx Z_{h}^{\star}+O(p^{2})$, under which the
weighted estimator has lower variance than the unweighted mean
when $Z_{h}$ varies across the momentum grid.

\paragraph{Updated records pointer (v0.3--v0.8).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}: theory tags
      \texttt{Math46c-c2-extractor-v0.3-2026-04-16} \ldots
      \texttt{Math46c-c2-extractor-v0.8-2026-04-16}.
\item \texttt{PDE/stamp\_version\_headers.py}:
      \texttt{math46\_c2\_extractor.py = v0.8}.
\item \texttt{Website/data/version\_index.json}: current tag
      \texttt{Math46c-c2-extractor-v0.8-2026-04-16}.
\end{itemize}

\end{document}

% =========================================================
%  TECT -- Math47 research note (2026-04-16)
%  Mixed metric-gauge (h--F) bilinear response and the
%  equivalence-principle closure of the Math45 / Math44
%  couplings.
%
%  Purpose:
%    Math45 defines the graviton kinetic coefficient
%    kappa_G^{-2} = Y q_0^2 = |Z|/2 from the pure TT block
%    of the projected Hessian (Math46c T2).  Math44 defines
%    the Yang-Mills kinetic coefficients (c_W, c_B) from the
%    pure gauge-probe response (Math46b T6).  Neither alone
%    establishes that matter couples to gravity with the
%    same kappa_G -- that is the TECT analogue of the
%    equivalence principle and must be checked at the
%    mixed bilinear level.
%
%    Math47 defines the mixed (h, a_mu) bilinear-response
%    vertex at the Brazovskii-locked vacuum, proves a Ward-
%    type identity that forces the vertex to take the form
%    (graviton) x (gauge stress-energy) x (kappa_G), and
%    specifies the joint-closure audit T7 that any Math46c /
%    Math46b-compliant extractor pair must pass.
%
%  Feeds: Math44 Thm cWcB; Math45 Thm kappaG; Math46b §5
%         (E1-E7); Math46c §7 (Steps 1-5).

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,amsthm}
\newtheorem{thm}{Theorem}
\newtheorem{lem}[thm]{Lemma}
\newtheorem{prop}[thm]{Proposition}
\newtheorem{cor}[thm]{Corollary}
\theoremstyle{definition}
\newtheorem{defn}[thm]{Definition}
\theoremstyle{remark}
\newtheorem*{rmk}{Remark}
\begin{document}

\section*{Math47: Mixed metric--gauge bilinear response and the
equivalence-principle closure of $(\kappa_G,c_W,c_B)$}

\subsection*{0. Motivation}

The Math45 / Math46c audit extracts the graviton kinetic
coefficient $\kappa_G^{-2}=Yq_0^{2}=|Z|/2$ from the transverse-
traceless block of the projected Hessian with symmetric-tensor
probes acting on the locked condensate. The Math44 / Math46b
audit extracts the Yang--Mills coefficients
$c_W=1/(96\pi^{2})$, $c_B=1/(64\pi^{2})$ from gauge-plane-wave
probes of the one-loop $\tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log$. Neither audit,
taken separately, establishes that the emergent $SU(2)_W\times
U(1)_Y$ gauge fields couple to the emergent graviton with the
universal strength $\kappa_G$ demanded by the equivalence
principle. The universal coupling must be read off the
\emph{mixed} $\partial^{2}S_{\mathrm{eff}}/\partial\varepsilon_h
\,\partial\varepsilon_a$ bilinear vertex at $a=0,h=0$.

\subsection*{1. Mixed probe on the locked vacuum}

\begin{defn}[Mixed metric--gauge probe]
\label{defn:mixed-probe}
Fix a probe momentum $p$ with $|p|\ll q_0$, orthonormal triad
$(\hat p,\hat e_1,\hat e_2)$, and TT polarisation
$E\in\{E^{(TT1)},E^{(TT2)}\}$ (Math46c Def probe-basis). Fix a
gauge polarisation $(\hat{\epsilon}^{a}_\mu,\hat{\epsilon}^{0}_\mu)$
with $\hat\epsilon\cdot p=0$ and a second momentum $q$ with
$|q|\lesssim q_0$. Define the two-parameter deformation of the
locked package:
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{\varepsilon_h,\varepsilon_a}(x)
 \;:=\;
 \Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}\!\bigl((I+\varepsilon_h E\cos(p\!\cdot\!x))\,x\bigr)
 \,\mathrm{Pexp}\!\left[
   i\,\varepsilon_a\!\int^{x}\! a_\mu(y)\,dy^{\mu}
 \right],
\label{eq:mixed-def}
\end{equation}
with $a_\mu(y)=[\hat\epsilon^{a}_\mu T^{a}+
\hat\epsilon^{0}_\mu Y]\cos(q\cdot y)$.
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[Mixed bilinear vertex]
\label{defn:Gamma3}
Let $S_{\mathrm{eff}}$ be the Math46b $\tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log$
effective action on the Brazovskii shell. The mixed bilinear
response at the locked vacuum is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(h,a,a)}(p;q_1,q_2)
 \;:=\;
 \frac{1}{V}\,
 \frac{\partial^{3}S_{\mathrm{eff}}}
      {\partial\varepsilon_h\,\partial\varepsilon_a(q_1)\,
       \partial\varepsilon_a(q_2)}
 \Bigg|_{\varepsilon_h=\varepsilon_a=0},
\label{eq:Gamma3-def}
\end{equation}
evaluated with momentum conservation $p+q_1+q_2=0$.
\end{defn}

\begin{rmk}
$\Gamma^{(h,a,a)}$ is the on-shell three-point function between
one graviton polarisation and two gauge-probe polarisations;
it is the lowest-order vertex sensitive to \emph{how strongly}
the gauge sector gravitates.
\end{rmk}

\subsection*{2. Ward identity and vertex structure}

\begin{lem}[Diffeomorphism Ward identity]
\label{lem:Ward}
Under the infinitesimal diffeomorphism
$x^{\mu}\to x^{\mu}+\xi^{\mu}(x)$ with
$\xi^{\mu}(x)=\zeta^{\mu}\cos(p\!\cdot\!x)$, $\zeta\cdot p=0$,
the effective action satisfies
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\xi}S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a,h]
 \;=\;-\int\!d^{3}x\;\xi^{\mu}\,\partial^{\nu}T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu}[a]
 \;+\;O(\xi^{2}),
\end{equation}
where $T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu}[a]$ is the gauge-sector stress tensor
determined by Math44 \S 4 (and depending on $(c_W,c_B)$ through
its normalisation).
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The locked vacuum preserves three-translation invariance; the
diffeomorphism $\xi$ acts on $\Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}$ as a pure
coordinate reparametrisation and therefore leaves the
family-and-locking part of $S_{\mathrm{eff}}$ invariant. The
gauge-source part transforms covariantly; integrating by parts
and using on-shell gauge invariance yields the stated divergence
of $T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[Forced vertex structure]
\label{prop:vertex}
The bilinear vertex (\ref{eq:Gamma3-def}) is forced by
Lem~\ref{lem:Ward} into the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(h,a,a)}_{\alpha,\hat\epsilon_1,\hat\epsilon_2}(p;q_1,q_2)
 \;=\;
 \kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}\,
 E^{(\alpha)}_{\mu\nu}\,
 T^{(a),\mu\nu}_{\hat\epsilon_1,\hat\epsilon_2}(q_1,q_2)
 \,+\,O(p^{2}),
\label{eq:vertex-form}
\end{equation}
with $T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu}$ the on-shell gauge stress tensor
normalised by $(c_W,c_B)$ of Math44, and $\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}$
the effective gravitational coupling read off the mixed vertex.
\end{prop}

\begin{thm}[Equivalence-principle identity]
\label{thm:EP}
On the Math40 locked triple, at the Math43 matching scale
$\ell^{\star}=1$, with $(c_W,c_B)$ satisfying Math44 Thm
\textnormal{cWcB} and $Z_h=Yq_0^{2}=|Z|/2$ satisfying Math45
Thm \textnormal{kappaG},
\begin{equation}
\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}} \;=\; \kappa_G \;\equiv\;
\sqrt{2/|Z|}.
\label{eq:EP}
\end{equation}
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
Equation~(\ref{eq:mixed-def}) places the gauge plane wave on
the $(I+\varepsilon_h E)$-deformed lattice. Expanding
$\tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log[-D_a^{2}+U''(\rho_D)]$ simultaneously
in $\varepsilon_h,\varepsilon_a$ and projecting onto the TT
sector:
\[
\frac{\partial^{3}S_{\mathrm{eff}}}
     {\partial\varepsilon_h\partial\varepsilon_a^{2}}
 =
 \frac{\partial^{2}}{\partial\varepsilon_a^{2}}
 \Bigl[\,
   \tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log\!\bigl(-D_a^{2}+U''(\rho_D)\bigr)
   \Bigr|_{g=I+\varepsilon_h E}
 \Bigr]_{\!\varepsilon_a=0}.
\]
The derivative with respect to the background metric is, by the
standard heat-kernel identity, the trace of the stress tensor
weighted by $E$:
\[
\frac{\partial S_{\mathrm{eff}}[a]}{\partial g^{\mu\nu}}
 = \tfrac12\,T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu}[a].
\]
Contracting with $E^{\mu\nu}$ and comparing to the pure-$h$
TT kinetic term $Z_h p^{2}\,(E\!\cdot\!E)$ of Math46c T2 gives
$\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}=\kappa_G$ to $O(p^2)$ corrections.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{3. Operational audit T7}

\begin{defn}[Mixed-response coefficient]
\label{defn:kappa-mix}
Let $E=E^{(TT1)}$ and $\hat\epsilon_{1,2}$ be transverse gauge
polarisations. Then
\begin{equation}
\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}
 \;:=\;
 \lim_{p,q\to 0}\,
 \frac{\Gamma^{(h,a,a)}_{TT,\hat\epsilon_1,\hat\epsilon_2}(p;q,-p-q)}
      {E^{\mu\nu}\,T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu,\hat\epsilon_1,\hat\epsilon_2}
         (q,-p-q)}.
\label{eq:kappa-mix-def}
\end{equation}
The denominator is evaluated with the Math46b-extracted
$(c_W,c_B)$, not with their Math44 target values (so T7 is not
circular).
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[T7: equivalence-principle closure]
\label{defn:T7}
The \emph{equivalence-principle defect} is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{EP}}
 \;:=\;
 \frac{\lvert\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}-\kappa_G\rvert}
      {\kappa_G}
 \;\stackrel{!}{\le}\;10^{-2},
\qquad
\kappa_G\;=\;\sqrt{2/|Z|}.
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

\begin{prop}[T7 failure modes]
\label{prop:T7fail}
T7 is falsified on refined grids $N\in\{32,64,128\}$ if any of
the following occurs:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(E1)] $\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}(N)$ does not converge to
      $\kappa_G$ at rate $\ge O(N^{-2})$.
\item[(E2)] The mixed vertex has a non-Ward component
      $\Gamma^{(h,a,a)}-\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}\,E\!\cdot\!T^{(a)}$
      whose Frobenius norm exceeds $10^{-2}$ of the leading
      term.
\item[(E3)] $\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}$ extracted from the
      $SU(2)_W$ sector and from the $U(1)_Y$ sector differ by
      more than $1\%$ after polarisation averaging.
\end{enumerate}
Any of (E1)--(E3) refutes the equivalence principle as an
emergent TECT statement and therefore invalidates the joint
Math44/Math45 closure.
\end{prop}

\subsection*{4. Joint extractor interface}

T7 is not computable from either the Math46c C2 extractor or
the Math46b C3 extractor alone. A faithful Math47-compliant
\emph{joint} extractor (tag: C2--C3 mixed) must expose:

\begin{description}
\item[\textbf{J1.}] Load the same solver package (Math46c P1,
Math46b E1).
\item[\textbf{J2.}] Load the same actual backend adapter
(Math46c P2, Math46b E5).
\item[\textbf{J3.}] Construct the mixed probe family
$\{v_{E,p}\otimes a_\mu(q)\}$ by composing the geometric
affine deformation (Math46c Def tangent) with the path-ordered
gauge exponential (Math46b Eq.~$F_a$-def). At $O(\varepsilon_h
\varepsilon_a^{2})$ the composition reduces to FFT-resampled
plane waves in both $p$ and $q$.
\item[\textbf{J4.}] Compute
$\partial^{3}S_{\mathrm{eff}}/\partial\varepsilon_h
\partial\varepsilon_a^{2}$ by a three-point finite difference
with $\varepsilon_h=\varepsilon_a=10^{-5}$, using Hutchinson
stochastic-trace-log with $N_s\sim 32$ samples on the shell
$\Sigma_{q_0,\Delta}$.
\item[\textbf{J5.}] Extract $\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}$ via
Def~\ref{defn:kappa-mix} using the Math46b-extracted
$(c_W,c_B)$ in the denominator, and emit $\Delta_{\mathrm{EP}}$
plus Ward-residual diagnostics per Prop~\ref{prop:T7fail}.
\end{description}

\subsection*{5. Consistency with Math40--Math46c}

\begin{thm}[Math47 closure with locked triple]
\label{thm:M47-closure}
Under Math40 locked $(\mu^{2},\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,+1.62)$,
$(Z,Y)=(-1,+\tfrac12)$, $\ell^{\star}=1$:
\begin{equation}
\kappa_G \;=\; \sqrt{2/|Z|}\;=\;\sqrt{2},
\qquad
\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}/\kappa_G \;=\; 1 \pm O(N^{-2}).
\end{equation}
Conversely, if the Math46b audit yields $(c_W,c_B)$ at their
Math44 values and the Math46c audit yields $Z_h=|Z|/2$, but T7
reports $\Delta_{\mathrm{EP}}>10^{-2}$ in the continuum limit,
then one of the two individual audits is secretly absorbing a
compensating error (a ``non-minimal coupling'' artefact) and
both claims must be revisited.
\end{thm}

\subsection*{6. Cost budget}

Per probe pair $(p,q)$: one $O(\varepsilon^{0})$ + three
$O(\varepsilon)$ evaluations of $\tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log
L_{\mathrm{full}}$ with Hutchinson $N_s\sim 32$. Multiply by
$n_{\mathrm{pol}}=3$ (TT pair + two TT rotations of $p$) and
$n_q=3$ (three transverse gauge polarisations $\hat\epsilon$)
and $n_{\mathrm{grid}}=3$ ($N\in\{32,64,128\}$):
\begin{equation}
C_{\mathrm{T7}}
 \;\approx\;4\cdot N_s\cdot n_{\mathrm{pol}}\cdot n_q
 \cdot n_{\mathrm{grid}}\cdot C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N)
 \;\approx\;1150\cdot C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N).
\end{equation}
At $N=128$ on a single A100 this is $\sim 20$--$24$ h
wall-clock. Combined with Math46b ($\sim 3$--$4$ h) and Math46c
($\sim 0.5$ h), the full closure audit fits in a two-day
campaign on one A100.

\subsection*{7. What remains (Math47 residual)}

(a) The Hutchinson variance on a third-order derivative scales
worse than on the second-order derivative of Math46b; the
stochastic sample budget $N_s$ may need to be increased to
$\sim 64$--$128$ for the $1\%$ audit threshold. A variance
pilot at $N=32$ is cheap and should precede the $N=128$ run.

(b) The gauge stress tensor $T^{(a)}_{\mu\nu}$ on a curved
on-grid metric requires the covariant plaquette definition of
Math46b E5 evaluated on the deformed lattice
$(I+\varepsilon_h E)$; the leading-order expansion is well-
defined but the error cancellation at
$O(\varepsilon_h^{2},\varepsilon_a^{2})$ must be verified
empirically.

(c) Math47 establishes closure at the one-loop bilinear level
only. Non-linear $(h^{2} a^{2})$ and $(h a^{4})$ vertices --
graviton self-coupling and higher gauge--graviton mixing --
are deferred to Math48 (non-linear Einstein--Hilbert closure).

\subsection*{8. Records pointers}

\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{CHANGELOG.md}: theory tag
      \texttt{Math47-mixed-hF-closure-2026-04-16}.
\item \texttt{docs/math/TECT-Math46b.tex.txt} \S 7(c):
      curved-background probe supplement now consumed by
      Math47 Def mixed-probe.
\item \texttt{docs/math/TECT-Math46c.tex.txt} \S 9(c): joint
      T2--T6 closure promise now superseded by the stronger
      T7 closure established here.
\item Joint extractor interface J1--J5 (§4) is the hard
      prerequisite for any ``Math47-compliant'' code deposit;
      as with Math46b/Math46c, no scaffolded code is written
      until the user-supplied Python skeleton arrives.
\end{itemize}

\end{document}

%    kappa_G at the h a a vertex.  This is one-loop and

%    the non-linear structure of emergent gravity also
%    matches Einstein-Hilbert:
%      (i)  the cubic graviton self-vertex must equal the
%           GR h^3 vertex with the same kappa_G;
%      (ii) the h^2 a^2 vertex must equal the GR expansion of
%           sqrt(-g) F_{mn} F^{mn} with the same kappa_G and
%           the same (c_W, c_B);
%      (iii) non-linear diffeomorphism invariance (second-
%           order Ward / Zinn-Justin identity) must hold.
%    Math48 formalises these three statements as operational
%    audits T8a / T8b / T8c on the same locked package, the
%    same actual backend Hessian, and (now) third and fourth
%    functional derivatives of S_eff.
%

%    Math44 (c_W, c_B), Math45 (kappa_G), Math46b/46c/47
%    (bilinear closure), would establish a finite-lattice,
%    numerical matching, at one-loop leading log and 1%
%    tolerance on the soft-mode window, between the
%    Brazovskii-locked IR effective action and
%    Einstein-Hilbert + SU(2)_W x U(1)_Y Yang-Mills.  This
%    is a partial IR-matching result; it does not cover the
%    fermion sector (Math49, reserved), the cosmological
%    constant (Math50, reserved), higher-loop corrections,
%    or any claim about ultraviolet completion.

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,amsthm}
\newtheorem{thm}{Theorem}
\newtheorem{lem}[thm]{Lemma}
\newtheorem{prop}[thm]{Proposition}
\newtheorem{cor}[thm]{Corollary}
\theoremstyle{definition}
\newtheorem{defn}[thm]{Definition}
\theoremstyle{remark}
\newtheorem*{rmk}{Remark}
\begin{document}

\section*{Math48: Cubic graviton self-vertex and the $h^{2}a^{2}$
vertex: non-linear IR matching to Einstein--Hilbert on the
Brazovskii-locked vacuum}

\subsection*{0. Motivation}

Math47 established $\kappa_G^{\mathrm{mix}}=\kappa_G$ at the
bilinear $h\,a\,a$ vertex; this is a statement about one
graviton insertion into the gauge two-point function. A more
complete matching of the emergent IR effective action to
Einstein--Hilbert coupled to $SU(2)_W\!\times\!U(1)_Y$
Yang--Mills — restricted to the orders in $h$ accessible to
the one-loop effective action on the Brazovskii-locked
vacuum — requires checking higher graviton multiplicities.
Math48 audits the minimal next terms:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the pure cubic graviton vertex $\Gamma^{(hhh)}$ reproduces
the GR expansion of $\tfrac{1}{2\kappa_G^{2}}\!\int\!\sqrt{-g}R$
at $O(h^{3})$ with the \emph{same} $\kappa_G$;
\item the $h^{2}a^{2}$ vertex reproduces the GR expansion of
$\tfrac14\sqrt{-g}F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}$ at $O(h^{2}a^{2})$ with
the same $\kappa_G$ and the same $(c_W,c_B)$ as Math44;
\item the non-linear diffeomorphism Ward identity (second-order
consistency of Lem~47 `Ward') holds.
\end{enumerate}
Math48 operationalises these three statements.

\subsection*{1. Cubic geometric probe}

\begin{defn}[Triple affine deformation]
\label{defn:triple-probe}
Fix three probe momenta $p_{1},p_{2},p_{3}$ with
$p_{1}+p_{2}+p_{3}=0$ and $|p_{k}|\ll q_{0}$, orthonormal triads
$(\hat p_{k},\hat e_{1,k},\hat e_{2,k})$, and TT polarisations
$E_{k}\in\{E^{(TT1)}_{k},E^{(TT2)}_{k}\}$ (Math46c Def
probe-basis). Define the three-parameter deformation
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{\varepsilon_{1},\varepsilon_{2},\varepsilon_{3}}(x)
 \;:=\;
 \Psi_{\mathrm{lock}}\!\bigl(\Phi_{\vec\varepsilon}(x)\bigr),
\qquad
\Phi_{\vec\varepsilon}(x)\;:=\;\Bigl(I\!+\!
\sum_{k=1}^{3}\varepsilon_{k}E_{k}\cos(p_{k}\!\cdot\!x)\Bigr)\,x.
\label{eq:triple-def}
\end{equation}
The composition is associative at $O(\varepsilon^{3})$; the
commutator of two affine deformations generates the $O(h^{2})$
diffeomorphism bracket required for the non-linear Ward identity
(Prop~\ref{prop:nonlin-Ward} below).
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[Cubic graviton vertex]
\label{defn:Gamma-hhh}
The cubic graviton vertex at the locked vacuum is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(hhh)}_{E_{1}E_{2}E_{3}}(p_{1},p_{2},p_{3})
 \;:=\;
 \frac{1}{V}\,
 \frac{\partial^{3}S_{\mathrm{eff}}}
      {\partial\varepsilon_{1}\,\partial\varepsilon_{2}\,
       \partial\varepsilon_{3}}
 \Bigg|_{\vec\varepsilon=0},
\end{equation}
evaluated on-shell with $p_{1}+p_{2}+p_{3}=0$.
\end{defn}

\subsection*{2. Einstein--Hilbert target}

\begin{lem}[GR cubic target]
\label{lem:GR-cubic}
The Einstein--Hilbert action
$S_{\mathrm{EH}}=\tfrac{1}{2\kappa_G^{2}}\!\int\!\sqrt{-g}R$
expanded on $g_{\mu\nu}=\eta_{\mu\nu}+\kappa_G h_{\mu\nu}$ yields,
in the transverse-traceless gauge $\partial^{\mu}h_{\mu\nu}=0$,
$h^{\mu}{}_{\mu}=0$,
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{EH}}^{(3)}[h]
 \;=\;\kappa_G\!\int\! d^{3}x\;
 \mathcal{V}^{\mu\nu\rho\sigma\alpha\beta}
 \bigl(\partial h\bigr)\bigl(\partial h\bigr)\bigl(\partial h\bigr),
\label{eq:GR-cubic}
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal{V}$ the standard Einstein cubic vertex kernel (a
homogeneous polynomial of degree two in momenta, degree six in
polarisations). Its closed form is tabulated in Appendix of
Goroff--Sagnotti (1986) and collapses on the TT shell to the
kinematic structure
$\mathcal{V}_{TT}(p_{1},p_{2},p_{3})
 =c_{1}p_{1}\!\cdot\!p_{2}\,E_{1}\!\cdot\!E_{3}\,E_{2}\!\cdot\!E_{3}
 +\text{perms}$
with the coefficient $c_{1}$ fixed by the Einstein normalisation
$1/(16\pi G_{N})=Z_{h}$.
\end{lem}

\begin{defn}[Cubic graviton ratio]
\label{defn:kappa3}
Define
\begin{equation}
\kappa_G^{(3)}\;:=\;
 \lim_{p\to 0}\,
 \frac{\Gamma^{(hhh)}_{E_{1}E_{2}E_{3}}(p_{1},p_{2},p_{3})}
      {\mathcal{V}^{\mathrm{GR}}_{E_{1}E_{2}E_{3}}(p_{1},p_{2},p_{3};\kappa_G=1)},
\end{equation}
where the denominator is the GR kinematic structure of
Lem~\ref{lem:GR-cubic} with $\kappa_G$ factored out. Then
$\kappa_G^{(3)}=\kappa_G$ is the non-linear Einstein-closure
statement.
\end{defn}

\subsection*{3. The $h^{2}a^{2}$ vertex}

\begin{defn}[$h^{2}a^{2}$ probe]
\label{defn:h2a2-probe}
Compose the double affine deformation $(E_{1},E_{2})$ of
Def~\ref{defn:triple-probe} (restricted to $k=1,2$) with the
Math46b plane-wave gauge probe at momenta $q_{1},q_{2}$,
$q_{1}+q_{2}=-p_{1}-p_{2}$. The quadri-bilinear response is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(hhaa)}_{E_{1}E_{2},\hat\epsilon_{1}\hat\epsilon_{2}}
 (p_{1},p_{2};q_{1},q_{2})
 \;:=\;
 \frac{1}{V}\,
 \frac{\partial^{4}S_{\mathrm{eff}}}
      {\partial\varepsilon_{h,1}\,\partial\varepsilon_{h,2}\,
       \partial\varepsilon_{a,1}\,\partial\varepsilon_{a,2}}
 \Bigg|_{\vec\varepsilon=0}.
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

\begin{lem}[GR $h^{2}a^{2}$ target]
\label{lem:GR-h2a2}
The expansion of $\tfrac14\sqrt{-g}F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}$ on
$g_{\mu\nu}=\eta_{\mu\nu}+\kappa_G h_{\mu\nu}$ at $O(h^{2}a^{2})$
yields
\begin{equation}
S^{(2,2)}[h,a]\;=\;\kappa_G^{2}\!\int\! d^{3}x\;
 \mathcal{W}^{\mu\nu\rho\sigma;\alpha\beta\gamma\delta}
 \,h_{\mu\nu}h_{\rho\sigma}\,
 \partial_{\alpha}a_{\beta}\partial_{\gamma}a_{\delta},
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal{W}$ the standard quadratic-in-metric coupling
kernel and overall normalisation $(c_W,c_B)$ entering through
the polarisation structure of the gauge field strength.
\end{lem}

\begin{defn}[$h^{2}a^{2}$ ratio]
\label{defn:kappa-mix2}
Define
\begin{equation}
\bigl(\kappa_G^{(2)}\bigr)^{2}
 \;:=\;
 \lim_{p,q\to 0}\,
 \frac{\Gamma^{(hhaa)}(p_{1},p_{2};q_{1},q_{2})}
      {\mathcal{W}^{\mathrm{GR}}(p_{1},p_{2};q_{1},q_{2};
         \kappa_G=1,c_W,c_B)},
\end{equation}
with $(c_W,c_B)$ in the denominator the Math46b-extracted
values.
\end{defn}

\subsection*{4. Non-linear Ward identity}

\begin{prop}[Second-order Ward / Zinn-Justin]
\label{prop:nonlin-Ward}
Under the second-order diffeomorphism
$x^{\mu}\to x^{\mu}+\xi^{\mu}+\tfrac12\xi^{\nu}\partial_{\nu}\xi^{\mu}
+O(\xi^{3})$ with $\xi^{\mu}=\zeta^{\mu}_{1}\cos p_{1}\!\cdot\!x+
\zeta^{\mu}_{2}\cos p_{2}\!\cdot\!x$, the effective action
satisfies
\begin{equation}
\delta^{(2)}_{\xi}S_{\mathrm{eff}}
 \;=\;
 \int\! d^{3}x\;
 \xi^{\mu}\xi^{\nu}\,
 \bigl[\partial_{\mu}\partial_{\nu}T^{(a)}_{\rho\sigma}
 -\text{anom}\bigr]\eta^{\rho\sigma}
 \;+\;O(\xi^{3}),
\end{equation}
where the anomalous piece $\mathrm{anom}$ must vanish in the
continuum limit for a consistent emergent geometry.
\end{prop}

\begin{defn}[Ward-consistency residual]
\label{defn:Ward-res}
The dimensionless Ward-consistency residual is
\begin{equation}
\Delta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{Ward}}
 \;:=\;
 \frac{\lVert\mathrm{anom}\rVert_{F}}
      {\lVert T^{(a)}\rVert_{F}\cdot\lVert\xi\rVert^{2}/\ell^{\star 2}}
 \;\stackrel{!}{\le}\;10^{-2}.
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

\subsection*{5. Operational audit T8}

\begin{defn}[T8a: cubic-graviton universality]
\label{defn:T8a}
\begin{equation}
\Delta^{(3)}_{\mathrm{EH}}
 \;:=\;
 \frac{\lvert\kappa_G^{(3)}-\kappa_G\rvert}{\kappa_G}
 \;\stackrel{!}{\le}\;10^{-2}.
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[T8b: $h^{2}a^{2}$ matching]
\label{defn:T8b}
\begin{equation}
\Delta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{hha}a}
 \;:=\;
 \frac{\lvert\kappa_G^{(2)}-\kappa_G\rvert}{\kappa_G}
 \;\stackrel{!}{\le}\;10^{-2}.
\end{equation}
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}[T8c: non-linear Ward consistency]
\label{defn:T8c}
$\Delta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{Ward}}\le 10^{-2}$ per
Def~\ref{defn:Ward-res}.
\end{defn}

\begin{prop}[T8 falsification modes]
\label{prop:T8fail}
T8 is falsified on refined grids $N\in\{32,64,128\}$ if any of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(H1)] $\kappa_G^{(3)}(N)$ does not converge to $\kappa_G$
      at rate $\ge O(N^{-2})$.
\item[(H2)] $\kappa_G^{(2)}(N)$ does not converge to $\kappa_G$
      at rate $\ge O(N^{-2})$.
\item[(H3)] $\Delta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{Ward}}(N)$ does not decrease
      as $N\to\infty$, signalling a persistent non-geometric
      anomaly.
\item[(H4)] $\kappa_G^{(3)}$ extracted from distinct TT
      polarisation triples differ by more than $1\%$ after BCC
      orbit averaging.
\end{enumerate}
Any of (H1)--(H4) refutes non-linear Einstein--Hilbert closure,
and, by Math47 Thm~\textnormal{EP}, also forces reinterpretation
of Math44/45/47.
\end{prop}

\subsection*{6. One-loop IR-matching proposition}

\begin{thm}[One-loop IR matching on the Brazovskii-locked vacuum]
\label{thm:IRmatch}
Let a Math48-compliant joint extractor, acting on a Math40
locked-triple solver package with Math43 matching scale
$\ell^{\star}=1$, satisfy:
\begin{itemize}
\item[(C1)] Math46c T1 purity, T2 Einstein normalisation
$Z_h=|Z|/2$, T3 universality on $N\in\{32,64,128\}$.
\item[(C2)] Math46b T6 with $c_W=1/(96\pi^{2})$,
$c_B=1/(64\pi^{2})$; gauge-isotropy $\le 1\%$.
\item[(C3)] Math47 T7 equivalence-principle defect
$\Delta_{\mathrm{EP}}\le 10^{-2}$.
\item[(C4)] Math48 T8a, T8b, T8c as defined above.
\end{itemize}
Then, at one-loop leading log and on the continuum-limit-
extrapolated scale, the IR effective action on the soft-mode
window $|p|\ll q_0$ admits the decomposition
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{IR}}
 \;=\;
 \frac{1}{2\kappa_G^{2}}\!\int\!\sqrt{-g}R
 \;-\;\frac{c_W}{4}\!\int\!\sqrt{-g}\,F^{a}_{\mu\nu}F^{a\,\mu\nu}
 \;-\;\frac{c_B}{4}\!\int\!\sqrt{-g}\,B_{\mu\nu}B^{\mu\nu}
 \;+\;\Delta S,
\end{equation}
with $\lVert\Delta S\rVert\le 10^{-2}\cdot\lVert S_{\mathrm{IR}}\rVert$
in operator norm on the soft-mode window. The theorem asserts a
numerical matching at the enumerated vertex orders only
(bilinear and cubic in $h$; bilinear in $a_\mu$; mixed $ha^2$
and $h^2 a^2$). It makes no claim about fermion content, the
cosmological-constant coefficient of $\sqrt{-g}$, two-loop or
higher corrections, operators outside the span of
(C1)--(C4), or the ultraviolet completion of the effective
theory. In abbreviated form: within the enumerated operator
set, the IR action matches Einstein--Hilbert $+$ electroweak
Yang--Mills with couplings $\kappa_G=\sqrt{2/|Z|}$ and
$(c_W,c_B)$ fixed by the Math40 triple, at a numerical
tolerance of $1\%$.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
The four conditions (C1)--(C4) each assert equality of a
specific coefficient of the one-loop $\tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log
L_{\mathrm{full}}$ expansion with its Einstein--Hilbert$+$YM
target to $\le 1\%$. The coefficients (C1)--(C4) are a spanning
set for the IR effective action at orders $(h^{2},h^{3},
h a^{2},h^{2}a^{2})$ with $a^{2}$ implicit. Any two actions
with matching coefficients on a spanning set of their IR
expansion differ by operators of higher mass dimension,
suppressed by $q_{0}/\Lambda_{\mathrm{UV}}$ — absorbed into
$\Delta S$ — or by operators that vanish by the Math47 Ward
identity (the diffeomorphism Lie bracket structure is already
enforced by Prop~\ref{prop:nonlin-Ward}).
\end{proof}

\subsection*{7. Joint extractor interface (J6--J9)}

Extending the Math47 interface:
\begin{description}
\item[\textbf{J6.}] Construct the triple affine deformation
      composition of Def~\ref{defn:triple-probe} on the locked
      package via FFT resampling, preserving associativity at
      $O(\varepsilon^{3})$.
\item[\textbf{J7.}] Evaluate the cubic derivative
      $\partial^{3}S_{\mathrm{eff}}/\partial\varepsilon^{3}$ by
      three-point finite difference with
      $\varepsilon=10^{-5}$; Hutchinson $N_{s}\ge 64$.
\item[\textbf{J8.}] Evaluate the quartic derivative
      $\partial^{4}S_{\mathrm{eff}}/
       \partial\varepsilon_{h}^{2}\partial\varepsilon_{a}^{2}$
      by two nested three-point stencils; require
      $N_{s}\ge 128$ to control variance.
\item[\textbf{J9.}] Compute $\Delta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{Ward}}$ by
      applying the second-order diffeomorphism
      $\xi+\tfrac12\xi\partial\xi$ to the probe and checking
      that $\delta^{(2)}_{\xi}S_{\mathrm{eff}}$ reduces to the
      stress-tensor bilinear up to the tolerated anomaly.
\end{description}

\subsection*{8. Cost budget}

Per cubic-graviton configuration: 8 evaluations
($\pm\varepsilon$ on three axes) of
$\tfrac12\mathrm{Tr}\log L_{\mathrm{full}}$ at Hutchinson
$N_s=64$. Per $h^{2}a^{2}$ configuration: 16 evaluations at
$N_s=128$. With $\sim 10$ kinematic configurations per grid
and three grids:
\begin{equation}
C_{\mathrm{T8}}
 \;\approx\;
 \bigl(8\!\cdot\!64 + 16\!\cdot\!128\bigr)\!\cdot\!10\!\cdot\!3
 \cdot C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N)
 \;\approx\;
 7.7\cdot 10^{4}\cdot C_{\mathrm{Hess}}(N).
\end{equation}
At $N=128$ on a single A100, $\sim 2$--$3$ weeks wall-clock,
or $\sim 2$--$3$ days on an 8$\times$A100 node. The full
Math40--Math48 closure campaign on a single node therefore
takes $\sim 1$ month single-A100 / $\sim 3$--$4$ days 8-A100.

\subsection*{9. Residual and deferred}

(a) Two-loop corrections to the TT graviton self-energy carry
unknown coefficient and would shift $\kappa_G^{(3)}$ by
$O(\hbar^{2})\sim O(1/q_{0}^{2})$. Math48 closure is a
\emph{one-loop} statement; claiming two-loop closure is
Math49 territory.

(b) The GR cubic vertex $\mathcal{V}$ of Lem~\ref{lem:GR-cubic}
is stated in continuum 3D (Euclidean); its BCC-lattice
discretisation carries finite-$N$ artefacts of order $O(1/N^{2})$.
The $N^{-2}$ Richardson extrapolation is assumed; if the
convergence rate departs from $N^{-2}$, the BCC $O_{h}$ artefact
structure must be modelled (Q-20 ticket).

(c) Fermion-sector IR matching (Math49, reserved: Dirac
operator on the locked vacuum and chiral-anomaly audit) is
independent of Math48 and is a prerequisite for any broader
Standard-Model-side matching claim. Math48 does not address
the fermion sector.

(d) The cosmological constant: Math48 fixes the coefficient of
$R$ but leaves the zero-derivative $\sqrt{-g}$ coefficient
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{cc}}$ unaudited. Math50 (vacuum-energy
cancellation via Math31 Class-III scalar sector) is reserved.

\end{itemize}
